 9283 
 9284   <category id="jniIntercept" label="JNI Function Interception">
 9285 
 9286     <intro>
 9287       Provides the ability to intercept and resend
 9288       Java Native Interface (JNI) function calls
 9289       by manipulating the JNI function table.
 9290       See <externallink id="jni/functions.html">JNI
 9291         Functions</externallink> in the <i>Java Native Interface Specification</i>.
 9292       <p/>
 9293       The following example illustrates intercepting the
 9294       <code>NewGlobalRef</code> JNI call in order to count reference
 9295       creation.
 9296       <example>
 9297 JNIEnv original_jni_Functions;
 9298 JNIEnv redirected_jni_Functions;
 9299 int my_global_ref_count = 0;
 9300 
 9301 jobject
 9302 MyNewGlobalRef(JNIEnv *jni_env, jobject lobj) {
 9303    ++my_global_ref_count;
 9304    return originalJNIFunctions-&gt;NewGlobalRef(env, lobj);
 9305 }
 9306 
 9307 void
 9308 myInit() {
 9309    jvmtiError err;
 9310 
 9311    err = (*jvmti_env)-&gt;GetJNIFunctionTable(jvmti_env, &amp;original_jni_Functions);
 9312    if (err != JVMTI_ERROR_NONE) {
 9313       die();
 9314    }
 9315    err = (*jvmti_env)-&gt;GetJNIFunctionTable(jvmti_env, &amp;redirected_jni_Functions);
 9316    if (err != JVMTI_ERROR_NONE) {
 9317       die();
 9318    }
 9319    redirectedJNIFunctions-&gt;NewGlobalRef = MyNewGlobalRef;
 9320       err = (*jvmti_env)-&gt;SetJNIFunctionTable(jvmti_env, redirected_jni_Functions);
 9321    if (err != JVMTI_ERROR_NONE) {
 9322       die();
 9323    }
 9324 }
 9325       </example>
 9326       Sometime after <code>myInit</code> is called the user's JNI
 9327       code is executed which makes the call to create a new global
 9328       reference.  Instead of going to the normal JNI implementation
 9329       the call goes to <code>myNewGlobalRef</code>.  Note that a
 9330       copy of the original function table is kept so that the normal
 9331       JNI function can be called after the data is collected.
 9332       Note also that any JNI functions which are not overwritten
 9333       will behave normally.
 9334       <todo>
 9335         check that the example compiles and executes.
 9336       </todo>
 9337     </intro>
 9338 
 9339     <function id="SetJNIFunctionTable" phase="start" num="120">
 9340       <synopsis>Set JNI Function Table</synopsis>
 9341       <description>
 9342         Set the JNI function table
 9343         in all current and future JNI environments.
 9344         As a result, all future JNI calls are directed to the specified functions.
 9345         Use <functionlink id="GetJNIFunctionTable"></functionlink> to get the
 9346         function table to pass to this function.
 9347         For this function to take effect the the updated table entries must be
 9348         used by the JNI clients.
 9349         Since the table is defined <code>const</code> some compilers may optimize
 9350         away the access to the table, thus preventing this function from taking
 9351         effect.
 9352         The table is copied--changes to the local copy of the
 9353         table have no effect.
 9354         This function affects only the function table, all other aspects of the environment are
 9355         unaffected.
 9356         See the examples <internallink id="jniIntercept">above</internallink>.
 9357       </description>
 9358       <origin>new</origin>
 9359       <capabilities>
 9360       </capabilities>
 9361       <parameters>
 9362         <param id="function_table">
 9363           <inptr>
 9364             <struct>jniNativeInterface</struct>
 9365           </inptr>
 9366           <description>
 9367             Points to the new JNI function table.
 9368           </description>
 9369         </param>
 9370       </parameters>
 9371       <errors>
 9372       </errors>
 9373     </function>
 9374 
 9375     <function id="GetJNIFunctionTable" phase="start" num="121">
 9376       <synopsis>Get JNI Function Table</synopsis>
 9377       <description>
 9378         Get the JNI function table.
 9379         The JNI function table is copied into allocated memory.
 9380         If <functionlink id="SetJNIFunctionTable"></functionlink>
 9381         has been called, the modified (not the original) function
 9382         table is returned.
 9383         Only the function table is copied, no other aspects of the environment
 9384         are copied.
 9385         See the examples <internallink id="jniIntercept">above</internallink>.
 9386       </description>
 9387       <origin>new</origin>
 9388       <capabilities>
 9389       </capabilities>
 9390       <parameters>
 9391         <param id="function_table">
 9392           <allocbuf>
 9393             <struct>jniNativeInterface</struct>
 9394           </allocbuf>
 9395           <description>
 9396             On return, <code>*function_table</code>
 9397             points a newly allocated copy of the JNI function table.
 9398           </description>
 9399         </param>
 9400       </parameters>
 9401       <errors>
 9402       </errors>
 9403     </function>

 9405   </category>

 9407   <category id="eventManagement" label="Event Management">

 9409     <function id="SetEventCallbacks" jkernel="yes" phase="onload" num="122">
 9410       <synopsis>Set Event Callbacks</synopsis>
 9411       <description>
 9412         Set the functions to be called for each event.
 9413         The callbacks are specified by supplying a replacement function table.
 9414         The function table is copied--changes to the local copy of the
 9415         table have no effect.
 9416         This is an atomic action, all callbacks are set at once.
 9417         No events are sent before this function is called.
 9418         When an entry is <code>NULL</code> or when the event is beyond
 9419         <paramlink id="size_of_callbacks"></paramlink> no event is sent.
 9420         Details on events are
 9421         described <internallink id="EventSection">later</internallink> in this document.
 9422         An event must be enabled and have a callback in order to be
 9423         sent--the order in which this function and
 9424         <functionlink id="SetEventNotificationMode"></functionlink>
 9425         are called does not affect the result.
 9426       </description>
 9427       <origin>new</origin>
 9428       <capabilities>
 9429       </capabilities>
 9430       <parameters>
 9431         <param id="callbacks">
 9432           <inptr>
 9433             <struct>jvmtiEventCallbacks</struct>
 9434             <nullok>remove the existing callbacks</nullok>
 9435           </inptr>
 9436           <description>
 9437             The new event callbacks.
 9438           </description>
 9439         </param>
 9440         <param id="size_of_callbacks">
 9441           <jint min="0"/>
 9442           <description>
 9443             <code>sizeof(jvmtiEventCallbacks)</code>--for version
 9444             compatibility.
 9445           </description>
 9446         </param>
 9447       </parameters>
 9448       <errors>
 9449       </errors>
 9450     </function>
 9451 
 9452     <function id="SetEventNotificationMode" jkernel="yes" phase="onload" num="2">
 9453       <synopsis>Set Event Notification Mode</synopsis>
 9454       <description>
 9455         Control the generation of events.
 9456         <constants id="jvmtiEventMode" label="Event Enable/Disable" kind="enum">
 9457           <constant id="JVMTI_ENABLE" num="1">
 9458             If <paramlink id="mode"></paramlink> is <code>JVMTI_ENABLE</code>,
 9459             the event <paramlink id="event_type"></paramlink> will be enabled
 9460           </constant>
 9461           <constant id="JVMTI_DISABLE" num="0">
 9462             If <paramlink id="mode"></paramlink> is <code>JVMTI_DISABLE</code>,
 9463             the event <paramlink id="event_type"></paramlink> will be disabled
 9464           </constant>
 9465         </constants>
 9466         If <code>event_thread</code> is <code>NULL</code>,
 9467         the event is enabled or disabled globally; otherwise, it is
 9468         enabled or disabled for a particular thread.
 9469         An event is generated for
 9470         a particular thread if it is enabled either at the thread or global
 9471         levels.
 9472         <p/>
 9473         See <internallink id="EventIndex">below</internallink> for information on specific events.
 9474         <p/>
 9475         The following events cannot be controlled at the thread
 9476         level through this function.
 9477         <ul>
 9478           <li><eventlink id="VMInit"></eventlink></li>
 9479           <li><eventlink id="VMStart"></eventlink></li>
 9480           <li><eventlink id="VMDeath"></eventlink></li>
 9481           <li><eventlink id="ThreadStart"></eventlink></li>
 9482           <li><eventlink id="CompiledMethodLoad"></eventlink></li>
 9483           <li><eventlink id="CompiledMethodUnload"></eventlink></li>
 9484           <li><eventlink id="DynamicCodeGenerated"></eventlink></li>
 9485           <li><eventlink id="DataDumpRequest"></eventlink></li>
 9486         </ul>
 9487         <p/>
 9488         Initially, no events are enabled at either the thread level
 9489         or the global level.
 9490         <p/>
 9491         Any needed capabilities (see Event Enabling Capabilities below) must be possessed
 9492         before calling this function.
 9493         <p/>
 9494         Details on events are
 9495         described <internallink id="EventSection">below</internallink>.
 9496       </description>
 9497       <origin>jvmdiClone</origin>
 9498       <eventcapabilities></eventcapabilities>
 9499       <parameters>
 9500         <param id="mode">
 9501           <enum>jvmtiEventMode</enum>
 9502           <description>
 9503             <code>JVMTI_ENABLE</code> or <code>JVMTI_DISABLE</code>
 9504           </description>
 9505         </param>
 9506         <param id="event_type">
 9507           <enum>jvmtiEvent</enum>
 9508           <description>
 9509             the event to control
 9510           </description>
 9511         </param>
 9512         <param id="event_thread">
 9513           <ptrtype>
 9514             <jthread impl="noconvert"/>
 9515             <nullok>event is controlled at the global level</nullok>
 9516           </ptrtype>
 9517             <description>
 9518               The thread to control
 9519             </description>
 9520         </param>
 9521         <param id="...">
 9522           <varargs/>
 9523             <description>
 9524               for future expansion
 9525             </description>
 9526         </param>
 9527       </parameters>
 9528       <errors>
 9529         <error id="JVMTI_ERROR_INVALID_THREAD">
 9530           <paramlink id="event_thread"/> is non-<code>NULL</code> and is not a valid thread.
 9531         </error>
 9532         <error id="JVMTI_ERROR_THREAD_NOT_ALIVE">
 9533           <paramlink id="event_thread"/> is non-<code>NULL</code> and is not live (has not been started or is now dead).
 9534         </error>
 9535         <error id="JVMTI_ERROR_ILLEGAL_ARGUMENT">
 9536           thread level control was attempted on events which do not
 9537           permit thread level control.
 9538         </error>
 9539         <error id="JVMTI_ERROR_MUST_POSSESS_CAPABILITY">
 9540           The Required Event Enabling Capability is not possessed.
 9541         </error>
 9542       </errors>
 9543     </function>
 9544 
 9545     <function id="GenerateEvents" num="123">
 9546       <synopsis>Generate Events</synopsis>
 9547       <description>
 9548         Generate events to represent the current state of the VM.
 9549         For example, if <paramlink id="event_type"/> is
 9550         <code>JVMTI_EVENT_COMPILED_METHOD_LOAD</code>,
 9551         a <eventlink id="CompiledMethodLoad"></eventlink> event will be
 9552         sent for each currently compiled method.
 9553         Methods that were loaded and now have been unloaded are not sent.
 9554         The history of what events have previously been sent does not
 9555         effect what events are sent by this function--for example,
 9556         all currently compiled methods
 9557         will be sent each time this function is called.
 9558         <p/>
 9559         This function is useful when
 9560         events may have been missed due to the agent attaching after program
 9561         execution begins; this function generates the missed events.
 9562         <p/>
 9563         Attempts to execute Java programming language code or
 9564         JNI functions may be paused until this function returns -
 9565         so neither should be called from the thread sending the event.
 9566         This function returns only after the missed events have been
 9567         sent, processed and have returned.
 9568         The event may be sent on a different thread than the thread
 9569         on which the event occurred.
 9570         The callback for the event must be set with
 9571         <functionlink id="SetEventCallbacks"></functionlink>
 9572         and the event must be enabled with
 9573         <functionlink id="SetEventNotificationMode"></functionlink>
 9574         or the events will not occur.
 9575         If the VM no longer has the information to generate some or
 9576         all of the requested events, the events are simply not sent -
 9577         no error is returned.
 9578         <p/>
 9579         Only the following events are supported:
 9580         <ul>
 9581           <li><eventlink id="CompiledMethodLoad"></eventlink></li>
 9582           <li><eventlink id="DynamicCodeGenerated"></eventlink></li>
 9583         </ul>
 9584       </description>
 9585       <origin>new</origin>
 9586       <capabilities>
 9587         <capability id="can_generate_compiled_method_load_events"></capability>
 9588       </capabilities>
 9589       <parameters>
 9590         <param id="event_type">
 9591           <enum>jvmtiEvent</enum>
 9592           <description>
 9593             The type of event to generate.  Must be one of these:
 9594             <ul>
 9595               <li><eventlink id="CompiledMethodLoad"><code>JVMTI_EVENT_COMPILED_METHOD_LOAD</code></eventlink></li>
 9596               <li><eventlink id="DynamicCodeGenerated"><code>JVMTI_EVENT_DYNAMIC_CODE_GENERATED</code></eventlink></li>
 9597             </ul>
 9598           </description>
 9599         </param>
 9600       </parameters>
 9601       <errors>
 9602         <error id="JVMTI_ERROR_MUST_POSSESS_CAPABILITY">
 9603           <paramlink id="event_type"/> is
 9604           <eventlink id="CompiledMethodLoad"><code>JVMTI_EVENT_COMPILED_METHOD_LOAD</code></eventlink>
 9605           and <fieldlink id="can_generate_compiled_method_load_events" struct="jvmtiCapabilities"></fieldlink>
 9606           is <code>false</code>.
 9607         </error>
 9608         <error id="JVMTI_ERROR_ILLEGAL_ARGUMENT">
 9609           <paramlink id="event_type"/> is other than
 9610           <eventlink id="CompiledMethodLoad"><code>JVMTI_EVENT_COMPILED_METHOD_LOAD</code></eventlink>
 9611           or <eventlink id="DynamicCodeGenerated"><code>JVMTI_EVENT_DYNAMIC_CODE_GENERATED</code></eventlink>.
 9612         </error>
 9613       </errors>
 9614     </function>
 9615 
 9616   </category>
 9617 
 9618     <category id="extension" label="Extension Mechanism">
 9619 
 9620       <intro>
 9621         These functions
 9622         allow a <jvmti/> implementation to provide functions and events
 9623         beyond those defined in this specification.
 9624         <p/>
 9625         Both extension functions and extension events have parameters
 9626         each of which has a 'type' and 'kind' chosen from the following tables:
 9627 
 9628         <constants id="jvmtiParamTypes" label="Extension Function/Event Parameter Types" kind="enum">
 9629           <constant id="JVMTI_TYPE_JBYTE" num="101">
 9630             Java programming language primitive type - <code>byte</code>.
 9631             JNI type <code>jbyte</code>.
 9632           </constant>
 9633           <constant id="JVMTI_TYPE_JCHAR" num="102">
 9634             Java programming language primitive type - <code>char</code>.
 9635             JNI type <code>jchar</code>.
 9636           </constant>
 9637           <constant id="JVMTI_TYPE_JSHORT" num="103">
 9638             Java programming language primitive type - <code>short</code>.
 9639             JNI type <code>jshort</code>.
 9640           </constant>
 9641           <constant id="JVMTI_TYPE_JINT" num="104">
 9642             Java programming language primitive type - <code>int</code>.
 9643             JNI type <datalink id="jint"></datalink>.
 9644           </constant>
 9645           <constant id="JVMTI_TYPE_JLONG" num="105">
 9646             Java programming language primitive type - <code>long</code>.
 9647             JNI type <datalink id="jlong"></datalink>.
 9648           </constant>
 9649           <constant id="JVMTI_TYPE_JFLOAT" num="106">
 9650             Java programming language primitive type - <code>float</code>.
 9651             JNI type <datalink id="jfloat"></datalink>.
 9652           </constant>
 9653           <constant id="JVMTI_TYPE_JDOUBLE" num="107">
 9654             Java programming language primitive type - <code>double</code>.
 9655             JNI type <datalink id="jdouble"></datalink>.
 9656           </constant>
 9657           <constant id="JVMTI_TYPE_JBOOLEAN" num="108">
 9658             Java programming language primitive type - <code>boolean</code>.
 9659             JNI type <datalink id="jboolean"></datalink>.
 9660           </constant>
 9661           <constant id="JVMTI_TYPE_JOBJECT" num="109">
 9662             Java programming language object type - <code>java.lang.Object</code>.
 9663             JNI type <datalink id="jobject"></datalink>.
 9664             Returned values are JNI local references and must be managed.
 9665           </constant>
 9666           <constant id="JVMTI_TYPE_JTHREAD" num="110">
 9667             Java programming language object type - <code>java.lang.Thread</code>.
 9668             <jvmti/> type <datalink id="jthread"></datalink>.
 9669             Returned values are JNI local references and must be managed.
 9670           </constant>
 9671           <constant id="JVMTI_TYPE_JCLASS" num="111">
 9672             Java programming language object type - <code>java.lang.Class</code>.
 9673             JNI type <datalink id="jclass"></datalink>.
 9674             Returned values are JNI local references and must be managed.
 9675           </constant>
 9676           <constant id="JVMTI_TYPE_JVALUE" num="112">
 9677             Union of all Java programming language primitive and object types -
 9678             JNI type <datalink id="jvalue"></datalink>.
 9679             Returned values which represent object types are JNI local references and must be managed.
 9680           </constant>
 9681           <constant id="JVMTI_TYPE_JFIELDID" num="113">
 9682             Java programming language field identifier -
 9683             JNI type <datalink id="jfieldID"></datalink>.
 9684           </constant>
 9685           <constant id="JVMTI_TYPE_JMETHODID" num="114">
 9686             Java programming language method identifier -
 9687             JNI type <datalink id="jmethodID"></datalink>.
 9688           </constant>
 9689           <constant id="JVMTI_TYPE_CCHAR" num="115">
 9690             C programming language type - <code>char</code>.
 9691           </constant>
 9692           <constant id="JVMTI_TYPE_CVOID" num="116">
 9693             C programming language type - <code>void</code>.
 9694           </constant>
 9695           <constant id="JVMTI_TYPE_JNIENV" num="117">
 9696             JNI environment - <code>JNIEnv</code>.
 9697             Should be used with the correct <datalink id="jvmtiParamKind"/> to make it a pointer type.
 9698           </constant>
 9699         </constants>
 9700 
 9701         <constants id="jvmtiParamKind" label="Extension Function/Event Parameter Kinds" kind="enum">
 9702           <constant id="JVMTI_KIND_IN" num="91">
 9703             Ingoing argument - <code>foo</code>.
 9704           </constant>
 9705           <constant id="JVMTI_KIND_IN_PTR" num="92">
 9706             Ingoing pointer argument - <code>const foo*</code>.
 9707           </constant>
 9708           <constant id="JVMTI_KIND_IN_BUF" num="93">
 9709             Ingoing array argument - <code>const foo*</code>.
 9710           </constant>
 9711           <constant id="JVMTI_KIND_ALLOC_BUF" num="94">
 9712             Outgoing allocated array argument -  <code>foo**</code>.
 9713             Free with <code>Deallocate</code>.
 9714           </constant>
 9715           <constant id="JVMTI_KIND_ALLOC_ALLOC_BUF" num="95">
 9716             Outgoing allocated array of allocated arrays argument - <code>foo***</code>.
 9717             Free with <code>Deallocate</code>.
 9718           </constant>
 9719           <constant id="JVMTI_KIND_OUT" num="96">
 9720             Outgoing argument - <code>foo*</code>.
 9721           </constant>
 9722           <constant id="JVMTI_KIND_OUT_BUF" num="97">
 9723             Outgoing array argument (pre-allocated by agent) - <code>foo*</code>.
 9724             Do not <code>Deallocate</code>.
 9725           </constant>
 9726         </constants>

 9728       </intro>

 9901               <struct>jvmtiParamInfo</struct>
 9902             </allocfieldbuf>

 9904               Array of

 9907             </description>
 9908           </field>
 9909         </typedef>

 9935       <callback id="jvmtiExtensionEvent">
 9936         <void/>
 9937           <synopsis>Extension Event</synopsis>
 9938         <description>
 9939           This is the implementation-specific event.
 9940           The event handler is set with
 9941           <functionlink id="SetExtensionEventCallback"/>.
 9942           <p/>
 9943           Event handlers for extension events must be declared varargs to match this definition.
 9944           Failure to do so could result in calling convention mismatch and undefined behavior
 9945           on some platforms.
 9946           <p/>
 9947           For example, if the <code>jvmtiParamInfo</code>
 9948           returned by <functionlink id="GetExtensionEvents"/> indicates that
 9949           there is a <code>jint</code> parameter, the event handler should be
 9950           declared:
 9951 <example>
 9952     void JNICALL myHandler(jvmtiEnv* jvmti_env, jint myInt, ...)
 9953 </example>
 9954           Note the terminal "<code>...</code>" which indicates varargs.
 9955         </description>
 9956         <parameters>
 9957           <param id="jvmti_env">
 9958             <outptr>
 9959               <struct>jvmtiEnv</struct>
 9960             </outptr>
 9961             <description>
 9962               The <jvmti/> environment is the only fixed parameter for extension events.
 9963             </description>
 9964           </param>
 9965           <param id="...">
 9966             <varargs/>
 9967               <description>
 9968                 The extension event-specific parameters
 9969               </description>
 9970           </param>
 9971         </parameters>
 9972       </callback>

 9979           enables the event. Or, if the callback is <code>NULL</code>, disables
 9980           the event.  Note that unlike standard events, setting
 9981           the callback and enabling the event are a single operation.
 9982         </description>

 9995               </description>
 9996           </param>

10000               <nullok>disable the event</nullok>

10021 
10022   <category id="capability" label="Capability">
10023 
10024     <intro>
10025       The capabilities functions allow you to change the
10026       functionality available to <jvmti/>--that is,
10027       which <jvmti/>
10028       functions can be called, what events can be generated,
10029       and what functionality these events and functions can
10030       provide.
10031       <p/>
10032         The "Capabilities" section of each function and event describe which
10033         capabilities, if any, they are associated with. "Required Functionality"
10034         means it is available for use and no capabilities must be added to use it.
10035         "Optional Functionality" means the agent must possess the capability
10036         before it can be used.
10037         To possess a capability, the agent must
10038         <functionlink id="AddCapabilities">add the capability</functionlink>.
10039         "Optional Features" describe capabilities which,
10040         if added, extend the feature set.
10041         <p/>
10042         The potentially available capabilities of each <jvmti/> implementation are different.
10043         Depending on the implementation, a capability:
10044         <ul>
10045           <li>may never be added</li>
10046           <li>may be added in either the <code>OnLoad</code> or live phase in any environment</li>
10047           <li>may be added only during the <code>OnLoad</code> phase</li>
10048           <li>may be possessed by only one environment at a time</li>
10049           <li>may be possessed by only one environment at a time,
10050               and only during the <code>OnLoad</code> phase</li>
10051           <li>and so on ...</li>
10052         </ul>
10053       Frequently, the addition of a capability may incur a cost in execution speed, start up
10054       time, and/or memory footprint.  Note that the overhead of using a capability
10055       is completely different than the overhead of possessing a capability.
10056       Take single stepping as an example. When single stepping is on (that
10057       is, when the event is enabled and thus actively sending events)
10058       the overhead of sending and processing an event
10059       on each instruction is huge in any implementation.
10060       However, the overhead of possessing the capability may be small or large,
10061       depending on the implementation.  Also, when and if a capability is potentially
10062       available depends on the implementation.  Some examples:
10063       <ul>
10064         <li>One VM might perform all execution by compiling bytecodes into
10065           native code and be unable to generate single step instructions.
10066           In this implementation the capability can not be added.</li>
10067         <li>Another VM may be able to switch execution to a single stepping
10068           interpreter at any time.  In this implementation, having the capability has no
10069           overhead and could be added at any time.</li>
10070         <li>Yet another VM might be able to choose a bytecode compiling or single stepping capable interpreted
10071           execution engine at start up, but be unable to switch between them.
10072           In this implementation the capability would need to be added
10073           during the <code>OnLoad</code> phase (before bytecode
10074           execution begins) and would have a large impact on execution speed
10075           even if single stepping was never used.</li>
10076         <li>Still another VM might be able to add an "is single stepping on" check
10077           into compiled bytecodes or a generated interpreter.  Again in this implementation
10078           the capability would need to be added during the <code>OnLoad</code> phase but the overhead (a test
10079           and branch on each instruction) would be considerably less.</li>
10080       </ul>
10081       <p/>
10082       Each <jvmti/> <internallink id="environments">environment</internallink>
10083       has its own set of capabilities.
10084       Initially, that set is empty.
10085       Any desired capability must be added.
10086       If possible, capabilities should be added during the <code>OnLoad</code> phase.  For most
10087       virtual machines certain capabilities require special set up for
10088       the virtual machine and this set up must happen
10089       during the <code>OnLoad</code> phase, before the virtual machine begins execution.
10090       Once a capability is added, it can
10091       only be removed if explicitly relinquished by the environment.
10092       <p/>
10093       The agent can,
10094       <functionlink id="GetPotentialCapabilities">determine what
10095         capabilities this VM can potentially provide</functionlink>,
10096       <functionlink id="AddCapabilities">add the capabilities
10097         to be used</functionlink>,
10098       <functionlink id="RelinquishCapabilities">release capabilities
10099         which are no longer needed</functionlink>, and
10100       <functionlink id="GetCapabilities">examine the currently available
10101         capabilities</functionlink>.
10102     </intro>
10103 
10104     <intro id="capabilityExamples" label="Capability Examples">
10105       For example, a freshly started agent (in the <code>OnLoad</code> function)
10106       wants to enable all possible capabilities.
10107       Note that, in general, this is not advisable as the agent may suffer
10108       a performance penalty for functionality it is not using.
10109       The code might look like this in C:
10110       <example>
10111         jvmtiCapabilities capa;
10112         jvmtiError err;
10113 
10114         err = (*jvmti)-&gt;GetPotentialCapabilities(jvmti, &amp;capa);
10115         if (err == JVMTI_ERROR_NONE) {
10116            err = (*jvmti)-&gt;AddCapabilities(jvmti, &amp;capa);
10117       </example>
10118       For example, if an  agent wants to check if it can get
10119       the bytecodes of a method (that is, it wants to check
10120       if it previously added this capability and has not
10121       relinquished it), the code might
10122       look like this in C:
10123       <example>
10124         jvmtiCapabilities capa;
10125         jvmtiError err;
10126 
10127         err = (*jvmti)-&gt;GetCapabilities(jvmti, &amp;capa);
10128         if (err == JVMTI_ERROR_NONE) {
10129            if (capa.can_get_bytecodes) { ... } }
10130       </example>
10131     </intro>
10132

10426     <function id="GetPotentialCapabilities" jkernel="yes" phase="onload" num="140">
10427       <synopsis>Get Potential Capabilities</synopsis>
10428       <description>
10429         Returns via <paramlink id="capabilities_ptr"></paramlink> the <jvmti/>
10430         features that can potentially be possessed by this environment
10431         at this time.
10432         The returned capabilities differ from the complete set of capabilities
10433         implemented by the VM in two cases: another environment possesses
10434         capabilities that can only be possessed by one environment, or the
10435         current <functionlink id="GetPhase">phase</functionlink> is live,
10436         and certain capabilities can only be added during the <code>OnLoad</code> phase.
10437         The <functionlink id="AddCapabilities"></functionlink> function
10438         may be used to set any or all or these capabilities.
10439         Currently possessed capabilities are included.
10440         <p/>
10441         Typically this function is used in the <code>OnLoad</code> function.
10442         Some virtual machines may allow a limited set of capabilities to be
10443         added in the live phase.
10444         In this case, the set of potentially available capabilities
10445         will likely differ from the <code>OnLoad</code> phase set.
10446         <p/>
10447         See the
10448         <internallink id="capabilityExamples">Capability Examples</internallink>.
10449       </description>
10450       <origin>new</origin>
10451       <capabilities>
10452       </capabilities>
10453       <parameters>
10454         <param id="capabilities_ptr">
10455           <outptr><struct>jvmtiCapabilities</struct></outptr>
10456           <description>
10457             On return, points to the <jvmti/> capabilities that may be added.
10458           </description>
10459         </param>
10460       </parameters>
10461       <errors>
10462       </errors>
10463     </function>
10464 
10465     <elide>
10466     <function id="EstimateCostOfCapabilities" phase="onload" num="141">
10467       <synopsis>Estimate Cost Of Capabilities</synopsis>
10468       <description>
10469         <issue>There is strong opposition to this function.  The concern is
10470           that it would be difficult or impossible to provide meaningful
10471           numbers, as the amount of impact is conditional on many factors
10472           that a single number could not represent.  There is doubt that
10473           conditional implementations would be used or are even a good idea.
10474           The thought is that release documentation for the implementation
10475           would be the best means of exposing this information.
10476           Unless new arguments are presented, I intend to remove this
10477           function in the next revision.
10478         </issue>
10479         <p/>
10480         Return via the <paramlink id="time_impact_ptr"></paramlink> and
10481         <paramlink id="space_impact_ptr"></paramlink> an estimate of the impact
10482         of adding the capabilities pointed to by
10483         <paramlink id="capabilities_ptr"></paramlink>.
10484         The returned estimates are in percentage of additional overhead, thus
10485         a time impact of 100 mean the application might run
10486         at half the speed.
10487         The estimates are very rough approximations and are not guaranteed.
10488         Note also, that the estimates are of the impact of having the
10489         capability available--when and if it is used the impact may be
10490         much greater.
10491         Estimates can be for a single capability or for a set of
10492         capabilities.  Note that the costs are not necessarily additive,
10493         adding support for one capability might make another available
10494         for free or conversely having two capabilities at once may
10495         have multiplicative impact.
10496         Estimates are relative to the current set of capabilities -
10497         that is, how much more impact given the currently possessed capabilities.
10498         <p/>
10499         Typically this function is used in the OnLoad function,
10500         some virtual machines may allow a limited set of capabilities to be
10501         added in the live phase.
10502         In this case, the set of potentially available capabilities
10503         will likely differ from the OnLoad phase set.
10504         <p/>
10505         See the
10506         <internallink id="capabilityExamples">Capability Examples</internallink>.
10507       </description>
10508       <origin>new</origin>
10509       <capabilities>
10510       </capabilities>
10511       <parameters>
10512         <param id="capabilities_ptr">
10513           <inptr><struct>jvmtiCapabilities</struct></inptr>
10514           <description>
10515             points to the <jvmti/> capabilities to evaluate.
10516           </description>
10517         </param>
10518         <param id="time_impact_ptr">
10519           <outptr><jint/></outptr>
10520           <description>
10521             On return, points to the estimated percentage increase in
10522             run time if this capability was added.
10523           </description>
10524         </param>
10525         <param id="space_impact_ptr">
10526           <outptr><jint/></outptr>
10527           <description>
10528             On return, points to the estimated percentage increase in
10529             memory space used if this capability was added.
10530           </description>
10531         </param>
10532       </parameters>
10533       <errors>
10534         <error id="JVMTI_ERROR_NOT_AVAILABLE">
10535           The desired capabilities are not even potentially available.
10536         </error>
10537       </errors>
10538     </function>
10539     </elide>
10540 
10541     <function id="AddCapabilities" jkernel="yes" phase="onload" num="142">
10542       <synopsis>Add Capabilities</synopsis>
10543       <description>
10544         Set new capabilities by adding the capabilities
10545         whose values are set to one (<code>1</code>) in
10546         <code>*</code><paramlink id="capabilities_ptr"></paramlink>.
10547         All previous capabilities are retained.
10548         Typically this function is used in the <code>OnLoad</code> function.
10549         Some virtual machines may allow a limited set of capabilities to be
10550         added in the live phase.
10551         <p/>
10552         See the
10553         <internallink id="capabilityExamples">Capability Examples</internallink>.
10554       </description>
10555       <origin>new</origin>
10556       <capabilities>
10557       </capabilities>
10558       <parameters>
10559         <param id="capabilities_ptr">
10560           <inptr><struct>jvmtiCapabilities</struct></inptr>
10561           <description>
10562             Points to the <jvmti/> capabilities to add.
10563           </description>
10564         </param>
10565       </parameters>
10566       <errors>
10567         <error id="JVMTI_ERROR_NOT_AVAILABLE">
10568           The desired capabilities are not even potentially available.
10569         </error>
10570       </errors>
10571     </function>
10572 
10573 
10574     <function id="RelinquishCapabilities" phase="onload" num="143">
10575       <synopsis>Relinquish Capabilities</synopsis>
10576       <description>
10577         Relinquish the capabilities
10578         whose values are set to one (<code>1</code>) in
10579         <code>*</code><paramlink id="capabilities_ptr"></paramlink>.
10580         Some implementations may allow only one environment to have a capability
10581         (see the <internallink id="capability">capability introduction</internallink>).
10582         This function releases capabilities
10583         so that they may be used by other agents.
10584         All other capabilities are retained.
10585         The capability will no longer be present in <functionlink id="GetCapabilities"></functionlink>.
10586         Attempting to relinquish a capability that the agent does not possess is not an error.
10587           <issue>
10588             It is possible for the agent to be actively using capabilities
10589             which are being relinquished.  For example, a thread is currently
10590             suspended and can_suspend is being relinquished or an event is currently
10591             enabled and can_generate_whatever is being relinquished.
10592             There are three possible ways we could spec this:
10593             <ul>
10594               <li>relinquish automatically releases them</li>
10595               <li>relinquish checks and returns some error code if held</li>
10596               <li>it is the agent's responsibility and it is not checked</li>
10597             </ul>
10598             One of these should be chosen.
10599           </issue>
10600       </description>
10601       <origin>new</origin>
10602       <capabilities>
10603       </capabilities>
10604       <parameters>
10605         <param id="capabilities_ptr">
10606           <inptr><struct>jvmtiCapabilities</struct></inptr>
10607           <description>
10608             Points to the <jvmti/> capabilities to relinquish.
10609           </description>
10610         </param>
10611       </parameters>
10612       <errors>
10613       </errors>
10614     </function>
10615 
10616 
10617 
10618     <function id="GetCapabilities" jkernel="yes" phase="any" num="89">
10619       <synopsis>Get Capabilities</synopsis>
10620         <description>
10621           Returns via <paramlink id="capabilities_ptr"></paramlink> the optional <jvmti/>
10622           features which this environment currently possesses.
10623           Each possessed capability is indicated by a one (<code>1</code>) in the
10624           corresponding field of the <internallink id="jvmtiCapabilities">capabilities
10625           structure</internallink>.
10626           An environment does not possess a capability unless it has been successfully added with
10627           <functionlink id="AddCapabilities"/>.
10628           An environment only loses possession of a capability if it has been relinquished with
10629           <functionlink id="RelinquishCapabilities"/>. Thus, this function returns the net result
10630           of the <code>AddCapabilities</code> and <code>RelinquishCapabilities</code> calls which
10631           have been made.
10632           <p/>
10633           See the
10634           <internallink id="capabilityExamples">Capability Examples</internallink>.
10635         </description>
10636       <origin>jvmdiClone</origin>
10637       <capabilities>
10638       </capabilities>
10639       <parameters>
10640         <param id="capabilities_ptr">
10641           <outptr><struct>jvmtiCapabilities</struct></outptr>
10642           <description>
10643             On return, points to the <jvmti/> capabilities.
10644           </description>
10645         </param>
10646       </parameters>
10647       <errors>
10648       </errors>
10649     </function>

10651   </category>

10654   <category id="timers" label="Timers">
10655 
10656       <intro>
10657         These functions provide timing information.
10658         The resolution at which the time is updated is not specified.
10659         They provides nanosecond precision, but not necessarily nanosecond accuracy.
10660         Details about the timers, such as their maximum values, can be accessed with
10661         the timer information functions.
10662       </intro>
10663 
10664       <typedef id="jvmtiTimerInfo" label="Timer Info">
10665         <description>
10666           The information function for each timer returns this data structure.
10667         </description>
10668         <field id="max_value">
10669           <jlong/>
10670             <description>
10671               The maximum value the timer can reach.
10672               After this value is reached the timer wraps back to zero.
10673               This is an unsigned value.  If tested or printed as a jlong (signed value)
10674               it may appear to be a negative number.
10675             </description>
10676         </field>
10677         <field id="may_skip_forward">
10678           <jboolean/>
10679           <description>
10680             If true, the timer can be externally adjusted and as a result skip forward.
10681             If false, the timer value will never increase faster than real time.
10682           </description>
10683         </field>
10684         <field id="may_skip_backward">
10685           <jboolean/>
10686           <description>
10687             If true, the timer can be externally adjusted and as a result skip backward.
10688             If false, the timer value will be monotonically increasing.
10689           </description>
10690         </field>
10691         <field id="kind">
10692           <enum>jvmtiTimerKind</enum>
10693           <description>
10694             The kind of timer.
10695             On a platform that does not distinguish between user and system time, <datalink
10696                  id="JVMTI_TIMER_TOTAL_CPU"><code>JVMTI_TIMER_TOTAL_CPU</code></datalink>
10697             is returned.
10698           </description>
10699         </field>
10700         <field id="reserved1">
10701           <jlong/>
10702             <description>
10703               Reserved for future use.
10704             </description>
10705         </field>
10706         <field id="reserved2">
10707           <jlong/>
10708             <description>
10709               Reserved for future use.
10710             </description>
10711         </field>
10712       </typedef>
10713 
10714       <intro>
10715         Where the timer kind is --
10716 
10717         <constants id="jvmtiTimerKind" label="Timer Kinds" kind="enum">
10718           <constant id="JVMTI_TIMER_USER_CPU" num="30">
10719             CPU time that a thread is in user mode.
10720           </constant>
10721           <constant id="JVMTI_TIMER_TOTAL_CPU" num="31">
10722             CPU time that a thread is in user or system mode.
10723           </constant>
10724           <constant id="JVMTI_TIMER_ELAPSED" num="32">
10725             Elapsed time.
10726           </constant>
10727         </constants>
10728       </intro>
10729 
10730     <function id="GetCurrentThreadCpuTimerInfo" callbacksafe="safe"  impl="innative notrace" phase="start" num="134">
10731       <synopsis>Get Current Thread CPU Timer Information</synopsis>
10732       <description>
10733         Get information about the
10734         <functionlink id="GetCurrentThreadCpuTime"/> timer.
10735         The fields of the <datalink id="jvmtiTimerInfo"/> structure
10736         are filled in with details about the timer.
10737         This information is specific to the platform and the implementation of
10738         <functionlink id="GetCurrentThreadCpuTime"/> and thus
10739         does not vary by thread nor does it vary

10743         and <functionlink id="GetThreadCpuTime"/> may differ, and thus the values
10744         returned by <code>GetCurrentThreadCpuTimerInfo</code>
10745         and <functionlink id="GetThreadCpuTimerInfo"/>
10746         may differ -- see <functionlink id="GetCurrentThreadCpuTime"/> for more information.
10747       </description>
10748       <origin>new</origin>

10759             returned by <functionlink id="GetCurrentThreadCpuTime"/>.
10760           </description>
10761         </param>
10762       </parameters>
10763       <errors>
10764       </errors>

10767     <function id="GetCurrentThreadCpuTime" callbacksafe="safe" impl="innative notrace" phase="start" num="135">
10768       <synopsis>Get Current Thread CPU Time</synopsis>
10769       <description>
10770             Return the CPU time utilized by the current thread.
10771             <p/>
10772             Note that the <functionlink id="GetThreadCpuTime"/>
10773             function provides CPU time for any thread, including
10774             the current thread. <code>GetCurrentThreadCpuTime</code>
10775             exists to support platforms which cannot
10776             supply CPU time for threads other than the current
10777             thread or which have more accurate information for
10778             the current thread (see
10779             <functionlink id="GetCurrentThreadCpuTimerInfo"/> vs
10780             <functionlink id="GetThreadCpuTimerInfo"/>).
10781             On many platforms this call will be equivalent to:
10782 <example>
10783   GetThreadCpuTime(env, NULL, nanos_ptr)
10784 </example>
10785       </description>
10786       <origin>new</origin>
10787       <capabilities>
10788         <required id="can_get_current_thread_cpu_time">
10789             Can get current thread CPU time.
10790             <p/>
10791             If this capability is enabled after threads have started,
10792             the implementation may choose any time up
10793             to and including the time that the capability is enabled
10794             as the point where CPU time collection starts.
10795             <p/>
10796             This capability must be potentially available on any
10797             platform where
10798             <internallink id="jvmtiCapabilities.can_get_thread_cpu_time"><code>can_get_thread_cpu_time</code></internallink>
10799             is potentially available.
10800         </required>
10801       </capabilities>
10802       <parameters>

10804           <outptr><jlong/></outptr>
10805           <description>
10806             On return, points to the CPU time used by this thread
10807             in nanoseconds.
10808             This is an unsigned value.  If tested or printed as a jlong (signed value)
10809             it may appear to be a negative number.
10810           </description>
10811         </param>
10812       </parameters>
10813       <errors>
10814       </errors>
10815     </function>

10978   <category id="classLoaderSearch" label="Class Loader Search">
10979 
10980     <intro>
10981       These functions allow the agent to add to the locations that a class loader searches for a class.
10982       This is useful for installing instrumentation under the correct class loader.
10983     </intro>
10984 
10985     <function id="AddToBootstrapClassLoaderSearch" jkernel="yes" phase="onload" num="149">
10986       <synopsis>Add To Bootstrap Class Loader Search</synopsis>
10987       <description>
10988           This function can be used to cause instrumentation classes to be defined by the
10989           bootstrap class loader. See <vmspec chapter="5.3.1"/>.
10990           After the bootstrap
10991           class loader unsuccessfully searches for a class, the specified platform-dependent
10992           search path <paramlink id="segment"/> will be searched as well. Only one segment may be specified in
10993           the <paramlink id="segment"/>. This function may be called multiple times to add multiple segments,
10994           the segments will be searched in the order that this function was called.
10995           <p/>
10996           In the <code>OnLoad</code> phase the function may be used to specify any platform-dependent
10997           search path segment to be searched after the bootstrap class loader unsuccessfully searches
10998           for a class. The segment is typically a directory or JAR file.
10999           <p/>
11000           In the live phase the <paramlink id="segment"/> may be used to specify any platform-dependent
11001           path to a <externallink id="jar/jar.html">
11002           JAR file</externallink>. The agent should take care that the JAR file does not
11003           contain any classes or resources other than those to be defined by the bootstrap
11004           class loader for the purposes of instrumentation.
11005           <p/>
11006           <vmspec/> specifies that a subsequent attempt to resolve a symbolic
11007           reference that the Java virtual machine has previously unsuccessfully attempted
11008           to resolve always fails with the same error that was thrown as a result of the
11009           initial resolution attempt. Consequently, if the JAR file contains an entry
11010           that corresponds to a class for which the Java virtual machine has
11011           unsuccessfully attempted to resolve a reference, then subsequent attempts to
11012           resolve that reference will fail with the same error as the initial attempt.
11013       </description>
11014       <origin>new</origin>
11015       <capabilities>
11016       </capabilities>
11017       <parameters>
11018         <param id="segment">
11019           <inbuf><char/></inbuf>
11020           <description>
11021             The platform-dependent search path segment, encoded as a
11022             <internallink id="mUTF">modified UTF-8</internallink> string.
11023           </description>
11024         </param>
11025       </parameters>
11026       <errors>
11027         <error id="JVMTI_ERROR_ILLEGAL_ARGUMENT">
11028           <paramlink id="segment"/> is an invalid path. In the live phase, anything other than an
11029            existing JAR file is an invalid path.
11030         </error>
11031       </errors>
11032     </function>
11033 
11034     <function id="AddToSystemClassLoaderSearch" jkernel="yes" phase="onload" num="151" since="1.1">
11035       <synopsis>Add To System Class Loader Search</synopsis>
11036       <description>
11037           This function can be used to cause instrumentation classes to be
11038           defined by the system class loader. See <vmspec chapter="5.3.2"/>.
11039           After the class loader unsuccessfully searches for a class, the specified platform-dependent search
11040           path <paramlink id="segment"/> will be searched as well. Only one segment may be specified in the
11041           <paramlink id="segment"/>. This function may be called multiple times to add multiple segments, the
11042           segments will be searched in the order that this function was called.
11043           <p/>
11044           In the <code>OnLoad</code> phase the function may be used to specify any platform-dependent
11045           search path segment to be searched after the system class loader unsuccessfully searches
11046           for a class. The segment is typically a directory or JAR file.
11047           <p/>
11048           In the live phase the <paramlink id="segment"/> is a platform-dependent path to a
11049           <externallink id="jar/jar.html">JAR file</externallink> to be
11050           searched after the system class loader unsuccessfully searches for a class. The agent should
11051           take care that the JAR file does not contain any classes or resources other than those to be
11052           defined by the system class loader for the purposes of instrumentation.
11053           <p/>
11054           In the live phase the system class loader supports adding a JAR file to be searched if
11055           the system class loader implements a method name <code>appendToClassPathForInstrumentation</code>
11056           which takes a single parameter of type <code>java.lang.String</code>. The method is not required
11057           to have <code>public</code> access.
11058           <p/>
11059           <vmspec/> specifies that a subsequent attempt to resolve a symbolic
11060           reference that the Java virtual machine has previously unsuccessfully attempted
11061           to resolve always fails with the same error that was thrown as a result of the
11062           initial resolution attempt. Consequently, if the JAR file contains an entry
11063           that corresponds to a class for which the Java virtual machine has
11064           unsuccessfully attempted to resolve a reference, then subsequent attempts to
11065           resolve that reference will fail with the same error as the initial attempt.
11066       </description>
11067       <origin>new</origin>
11068       <capabilities>
11069       </capabilities>
11070       <parameters>
11071         <param id="segment">
11072           <inbuf><char/></inbuf>
11073           <description>
11074             The platform-dependent search path segment, encoded as a
11075             <internallink id="mUTF">modified UTF-8</internallink> string.
11076           </description>
11077         </param>
11078       </parameters>
11079       <errors>
11080         <error id="JVMTI_ERROR_ILLEGAL_ARGUMENT">
11081           <paramlink id="segment"/> is an invalid path. In the live phase, anything other than an
11082            existing JAR file is an invalid path.
11083         </error>
11084         <error id="JVMTI_ERROR_CLASS_LOADER_UNSUPPORTED">
11085           Operation not supported by the system class loader.
11086         </error>
11087       </errors>
11088     </function>
11089 
11090   </category>
11091 
11092 
11093   <category id="props" label="System Properties">
11094 
11095     <intro>
11096       These functions get and set system properties.
11097     </intro>
11098 
11099     <function id="GetSystemProperties" phase="onload" num="130">
11100       <synopsis>Get System Properties</synopsis>
11101       <description>
11102         The list of VM system property keys which may be used with
11103         <functionlink id="GetSystemProperty"/> is returned.
11104         It is strongly recommended that virtual machines provide the
11105         following property keys:
11106         <ul>
11107           <li><code>java.vm.vendor</code></li>
11108           <li><code>java.vm.version</code></li>
11109           <li><code>java.vm.name</code></li>
11110           <li><code>java.vm.info</code></li>
11111           <li><code>java.library.path</code></li>
11112           <li><code>java.class.path</code></li>
11113         </ul>
11114         Provides access to system properties defined by and used
11115         by the VM.
11116         Properties set on the command-line are included.
11117         This allows getting and setting of these properties
11118         before the VM even begins executing bytecodes.
11119         Since this is a VM view of system properties, the set of available
11120         properties will usually be different than that
11121         in <code>java.lang.System.getProperties</code>.
11122         JNI method invocation may be used to access
11123         <code>java.lang.System.getProperties</code>.
11124         <p/>
11125         The set of properties may grow during execution.
11126       </description>
11127       <origin>new</origin>
11128       <capabilities>
11129       </capabilities>
11130       <parameters>
11131         <param id="count_ptr">
11132           <outptr><jint/></outptr>
11133           <description>
11134             On return, points to the number of property keys returned.
11135           </description>
11136         </param>
11137         <param id="property_ptr">
11138           <allocallocbuf outcount="count_ptr"><char/></allocallocbuf>
11139           <description>
11140             On return, points to an array of property keys, encoded as
11141             <internallink id="mUTF">modified UTF-8</internallink> strings.
11142           </description>
11143         </param>
11144       </parameters>
11145       <errors>
11146       </errors>
11147     </function>
11148 
11149     <function id="GetSystemProperty" phase="onload" num="131">
11150       <synopsis>Get System Property</synopsis>
11151       <description>
11152         Return a VM system property value given the property key.
11153         <p/>
11154         The function <functionlink id="GetSystemProperties"/>
11155         returns the set of property keys which may be used.
11156         The properties which can be retrieved may grow during
11157         execution.
11158         <p/>
11159         Since this is a VM view of system properties, the values
11160         of properties may differ from that returned by
11161         <code>java.lang.System.getProperty(String)</code>.
11162         A typical VM might copy the values of the VM system
11163         properties into the <code>Properties</code> held by
11164         <code>java.lang.System</code> during the initialization
11165         of that class. Thereafter any changes to the VM system
11166         properties (with <functionlink id="SetSystemProperty"/>)
11167         or the <code>java.lang.System</code> system properties
11168         (with <code>java.lang.System.setProperty(String,String)</code>)
11169         would cause the values to diverge.
11170         JNI method invocation may be used to access
11171         <code>java.lang.System.getProperty(String)</code>.
11172       </description>
11173       <origin>new</origin>
11174       <capabilities>
11175       </capabilities>
11176       <parameters>
11177         <param id="property">
11178           <inbuf><char/></inbuf>
11179           <description>
11180             The key of the property to retrieve, encoded as a
11181             <internallink id="mUTF">modified UTF-8</internallink> string.
11182           </description>
11183         </param>
11184         <param id="value_ptr">
11185           <allocbuf><char/></allocbuf>
11186           <description>
11187             On return, points to the property value, encoded as a
11188             <internallink id="mUTF">modified UTF-8</internallink> string.
11189           </description>
11190         </param>
11191       </parameters>
11192       <errors>
11193         <error id="JVMTI_ERROR_NOT_AVAILABLE">
11194           This property is not available.
11195           Use <functionlink id="GetSystemProperties"/> to find available properties.
11196         </error>

11248     <function id="GetPhase" jkernel="yes" phase="any" num="133">
11249       <synopsis>Get Phase</synopsis>
11250       <description>
11251           Return the current phase of VM execution.
11252           The phases proceed in sequence:
11253           <constants id="jvmtiPhase" label="Phases of execution" kind="enum">
11254             <constant id="JVMTI_PHASE_ONLOAD" num="1">
11255               <code>OnLoad</code> phase: while in the
11256               <internallink id="onload"><code>Agent_OnLoad</code></internallink>
11257               or, for statically linked agents, the <internallink id="onload">
11258               <code>Agent_OnLoad_&lt;agent-lib-name&gt;
11259               </code></internallink> function.
11260             </constant>
11261             <constant id="JVMTI_PHASE_PRIMORDIAL" num="2">
11262               Primordial phase: between return from <code>Agent_OnLoad</code>
11263               or <code>Agent_OnLoad_&lt;agent-lib-name&gt;</code> and the
11264               <code>VMStart</code> event.
11265             </constant>
11266             <constant id="JVMTI_PHASE_START" num="6">
11267               Start phase: when the <eventlink id="VMStart"><code>VMStart</code></eventlink> event
11268               is sent and until the <code>VMInit</code> event is sent.
11269             </constant>
11270             <constant id="JVMTI_PHASE_LIVE" num="4">
11271               Live phase: when the <eventlink id="VMInit"><code>VMInit</code></eventlink> event is sent
11272               and until the <eventlink id="VMDeath"></eventlink> event returns.
11273             </constant>
11274             <constant id="JVMTI_PHASE_DEAD" num="8">
11275               Dead phase: after the <eventlink id="VMDeath"></eventlink> event returns or after
11276               start-up failure.
11277             </constant>
11278           </constants>
11279           In the case of start-up failure the VM will proceed directly to the dead
11280           phase skipping intermediate phases and neither a <code>VMInit</code> nor
11281           <code>VMDeath</code> event will be sent.
11282           <p/>
11283           Most <jvmti/> functions operate only in the live phase.
11284           The following functions operate in either the <code>OnLoad</code> or live phases:
11285           <functionphaselist phase="onload"/>
11286           The following functions operate in only the <code>OnLoad</code> phase:
11287           <functionphaselist phase="onloadOnly"/>
11288           The following functions operate in the start or live phases:
11289           <functionphaselist phase="start"/>
11290           The following functions operate in any phase:
11291           <functionphaselist phase="any"/>
11292           JNI functions (except the Invocation API) must only be used in the start or live phases.
11293           <p/>
11294           Most <jvmti/> events are sent only in the live phase.
11295           The following events operate in others phases:
11296           <eventphaselist phase="start"/>
11297           <eventphaselist phase="any"/>
11298       </description>
11299       <origin>new</origin>
11300       <capabilities>
11301       </capabilities>
11302       <parameters>
11303         <param id="phase_ptr">
11304           <outptr><enum>jvmtiPhase</enum></outptr>
11305           <description>
11306             On return, points to the phase.
11307           </description>
11308         </param>
11309       </parameters>
11310       <errors>
11311       </errors>
11312     </function>

11314     <function id="DisposeEnvironment" jkernel="yes" phase="any" num="127">
11315       <synopsis>Dispose Environment</synopsis>
11316       <description>
11317         Shutdown a <jvmti/> connection created with JNI <code>GetEnv</code>
11318         (see <internallink id="environments"><jvmti/> Environments</internallink>).
11319         Dispose of any resources held by the environment.
11320         <issue>
11321             What resources are reclaimed? What is undone?
11322             Breakpoints,watchpoints removed?
11323         </issue>
11324         Threads suspended by this environment are not resumed by this call,
11325         this must be done explicitly by the agent.
11326         Memory allocated by this environment via calls to <jvmti/> functions
11327         is not released, this can be done explicitly by the agent
11328         by calling <functionlink id="Deallocate"/>.
11329         Raw monitors created by this environment are not destroyed,
11330         this can be done explicitly by the agent
11331         by calling <functionlink id="DestroyRawMonitor"/>.
11332         The state of threads waiting on raw monitors created by this environment
11333         are not affected.
11334         <p/>
11335         Any <functionlink id="SetNativeMethodPrefix">native method
11336         prefixes</functionlink> for this environment will be unset;
11337         the agent must remove any prefixed native methods before
11338         dispose is called.
11339         <p/>
11340         Any <internallink id="capability">capabilities</internallink>
11341         held by this environment are relinquished.
11342         <p/>
11343         Events enabled by this environment will no longer be sent, however
11344         event handlers currently running will continue to run.  Caution must
11345         be exercised in the design of event handlers whose environment may
11346         be disposed and thus become invalid during their execution.
11347         <p/>
11348         This environment may not be used after this call.
11349         This call returns to the caller.
11350       </description>
11351       <origin>new</origin>
11352       <capabilities>
11353       </capabilities>
11354       <parameters>
11355       </parameters>
11356       <errors>
11357       </errors>
11358     </function>

11557     <function id="GetJLocationFormat" phase="any" num="129">
11558       <synopsis>Get JLocation Format</synopsis>
11559       <description>
11560         Although the greatest functionality is achieved with location information
11561         referencing the virtual machine bytecode index, the definition of
11562         <code>jlocation</code> has intentionally been left unconstrained to allow VM
11563         implementations that do not have this information.
11564         <p/>
11565         This function describes the representation of <code>jlocation</code> used in this VM.
11566         If the returned format is <datalink id="JVMTI_JLOCATION_JVMBCI"></datalink>,
11567         <code>jlocation</code>s can
11568         be used as in indices into the array returned by
11569         <functionlink id="GetBytecodes"></functionlink>.
11570         <constants id="jvmtiJlocationFormat" label="JLocation Format Enumeration" kind="enum">
11571           <constant id="JVMTI_JLOCATION_JVMBCI" num="1">
11572             <code>jlocation</code> values represent virtual machine
11573             bytecode indices--that is, offsets into the
11574             virtual machine code for a method.
11575           </constant>
11576           <constant id="JVMTI_JLOCATION_MACHINEPC" num="2">
11577             <code>jlocation</code> values represent native machine
11578             program counter values.
11579           </constant>
11580           <constant id="JVMTI_JLOCATION_OTHER" num="0">
11581             <code>jlocation</code> values have some other representation.
11582           </constant>
11583         </constants>
11584       </description>
11585       <origin>new</origin>
11586       <capabilities>
11587       </capabilities>
11588       <parameters>
11589         <param id="format_ptr">
11590           <outptr><enum>jvmtiJlocationFormat</enum></outptr>
11591           <description>
11592             On return, points to the format identifier for <code>jlocation</code> values.
11593           </description>
11594         </param>
11595       </parameters>
11596       <errors>
11597       </errors>
11598     </function>

11601 
11602   <category id="heap_monitoring" label="Heap Monitoring">
11603     <function id="SetHeapSamplingInterval" phase="onload" num="156" since="11">
11604       <synopsis>Set Heap Sampling Interval</synopsis>
11605       <description>
11606         Generate a <eventlink id="SampledObjectAlloc"/> event when objects are allocated.
11607         Each thread keeps a counter of bytes allocated. The event will only be generated
11608         when that counter exceeds an average of <paramlink id="sampling_interval"></paramlink>
11609         since the last sample.
11610         <p/>
11611         Setting <paramlink id="sampling_interval"></paramlink> to 0 will cause an event to be
11612         generated by each allocation supported by the system once the new interval is taken into account.
11613         <p/>
11614         Note that updating the new sampling interval might take various number of allocations
11615         to provoke internal data structure updates.  Therefore it is important to
11616         consider the sampling interval as an average. This includes the interval 0, where events
11617         might not be generated straight away for each allocation.
11618       </description>
11619       <origin>new</origin>
11620       <capabilities>
11621         <required id="can_generate_sampled_object_alloc_events"></required>
11622       </capabilities>
11623       <parameters>
11624         <param id="sampling_interval">
11625           <jint/>
11626           <description>
11627             The sampling interval in bytes. The sampler uses a statistical approach to
11628             generate an event, on average, once for every <paramlink id="sampling_interval"/> bytes of
11629             memory allocated by a given thread.
11630             <p/>
11631             Once the new sampling interval is taken into account, 0 as a sampling interval will generate
11632             a sample for every allocation.
11633             <p/>
11634             Note: The overhead of this feature is directly correlated with the sampling interval.
11635             A high sampling interval, such as 1024 bytes, will incur a high overhead.
11636             A lower interval, such as 1024KB, will have a much lower overhead.  Sampling should only
11637             be used with an understanding that it may impact performance.
11638           </description>
11639         </param>
11640       </parameters>
11641       <errors>
11642         <error id="JVMTI_ERROR_ILLEGAL_ARGUMENT">
11643           <paramlink id="sampling_interval"></paramlink> is less than zero.
11644         </error>
11645       </errors>
11646     </function>
11647   </category>
11648 
11649 </functionsection>
11650 
11651 <errorsection label="Error Reference">
11652   <intro>
11653     Every <jvmti/> function returns a <b><code>jvmtiError</code></b> error code.
11654     <p/>
11655     It is the responsibility of the agent to call <jvmti/> functions with
11656     valid parameters and in the proper context (calling thread is attached,
11657     phase is correct, etc.).
11658     Detecting some error conditions may be difficult, inefficient, or
11659     impossible for an implementation.
11660     The errors listed in
11661     <internallink id="reqerrors">Function Specific Required Errors</internallink>
11662     must be detected by the implementation.
11663     All other errors represent the recommended response to the error
11664     condition.
11665   </intro>
11666 
11667   <errorcategory id="universal-error" label="Universal Errors">
11668     <intro>
11669       The following errors may be returned by any function
11670     </intro>
11671 
11672     <errorid id="JVMTI_ERROR_NONE" num="0">
11673       No error has occurred.  This is the error code that is returned
11674       on successful completion of the function.
11675     </errorid>
11676     <errorid id="JVMTI_ERROR_NULL_POINTER" num="100">
11677       Pointer is unexpectedly <code>NULL</code>.
11678     </errorid>
11679     <errorid id="JVMTI_ERROR_OUT_OF_MEMORY" num="110">
11680       The function attempted to allocate memory and no more memory was
11681       available for allocation.
11682     </errorid>
11683     <errorid id="JVMTI_ERROR_ACCESS_DENIED" num="111">
11684       The desired functionality has not been enabled in this virtual machine.
11685     </errorid>
11686     <errorid id="JVMTI_ERROR_UNATTACHED_THREAD" num="115">
11687       The thread being used to call this function is not attached
11688       to the virtual machine.  Calls must be made from attached threads.
11689       See <code>AttachCurrentThread</code> in the JNI invocation API.
11690     </errorid>
11691     <errorid id="JVMTI_ERROR_INVALID_ENVIRONMENT" num="116">
11692       The <jvmti/> environment provided is no longer connected or is
11693       not an environment.
11694     </errorid>
11695     <errorid id="JVMTI_ERROR_WRONG_PHASE" num="112">
11696       The desired functionality is not available in the current
11697         <functionlink id="GetPhase">phase</functionlink>.
11698       Always returned if the virtual machine has completed running.
11699     </errorid>
11700     <errorid id="JVMTI_ERROR_INTERNAL" num="113">
