11862 
11863 <eventsection label="Events">
11864   <intro label="Handling Events" id="eventIntro">
11865     Agents can be informed of many events that occur in application
11866     programs.
11867     <p/>
11868     To handle events, designate a set of callback functions with
11869     <functionlink id="SetEventCallbacks"></functionlink>.
11870     For each event the corresponding callback function will be
11871     called.
11872     Arguments to the callback function provide additional
11873     information about the event.
11874     <p/>
11875     The callback function is usually called from within an application
11876     thread. The <jvmti/> implementation does not
11877     queue events in any way. This means
11878     that event callback functions must be written
11879     carefully. Here are some general guidelines. See
11880     the individual event descriptions for further
11881     suggestions.
11882     <p/>
11883     <ul>
11884       <li>Any exception thrown during the execution of an event callback can
11885         overwrite any current pending exception in the current application thread.
11886         Care must be taken to preserve a pending exception
11887         when an event callback makes a JNI call that might generate an exception.
11888       </li>
11889       <li>Event callback functions must be re-entrant. The <jvmti/> implementation does
11890         not queue events. If an agent needs to process events one at a time, it
11891         can use a raw monitor inside the
11892         event callback functions to serialize event processing.
11893       </li>
11894       <li>Event callback functions that execute JNI's FindClass function to load
11895         classes need to note that FindClass locates the class loader associated
11896         with the current native method. For the purposes of class loading, an
11897         event callback that includes a JNI environment as a parameter to the
11898         callback will treated as if it is a native call, where the native method
11899         is in the class of the event thread's current frame.
11900       </li>
11901     </ul>
11902     <p/>
11903     Some <jvmti/> events identify objects with JNI references.
11904     All references
11905     in <jvmti/> events are JNI local references and will become invalid
11906     after the event callback returns.
11907     Unless stated otherwise, memory referenced by pointers sent in event
11908     callbacks may not be referenced after the event callback returns.
11909     <p/>
11910     Except where stated otherwise, events are delivered on the thread
11911     that caused the event.
11912     Events are sent at the time they occur.
11913     The specification for each event includes the set of
11914     <functionlink id="GetPhase">phases</functionlink> in which it can be sent;
11915     if an event triggering activity occurs during another phase, no event
11916     is sent.
11917     <p/>
11918     A thread that generates an event does not change its execution status
11919     (for example, the event does not cause the thread to be suspended).
11920     If an agent wishes the event to result in suspension, then the agent
11921     is responsible for explicitly suspending the thread with
11922     <functionlink id="SuspendThread"></functionlink>.
11923     <p/>
11924     If an event is enabled in multiple environments, the event will be sent
11925     to each agent in the order that the environments were created.
11926   </intro>
11927 
11928   <intro label="Enabling Events" id="enablingevents">
11929     All events are initially disabled.  In order to receive any
11930     event:
11931       <ul>
11932         <li>
11933           If the event requires a capability, that capability must
11934           be added with
11935           <functionlink id="AddCapabilities"></functionlink>.
11936         </li>
11937         <li>
11938           A callback for the event must be set with
11939           <functionlink id="SetEventCallbacks"></functionlink>.
11940         </li>
11941         <li>
11942           The event must be enabled with
11943           <functionlink id="SetEventNotificationMode"></functionlink>.
11944         </li>
11945       </ul>
11946   </intro>
11947 
11948   <intro label="Multiple Co-located Events" id="eventorder">
11949     In many situations it is possible for multiple events to occur
11950     at the same location in one thread. When this happens, all the events
11951     are reported through the event callbacks in the order specified in this section.
11952     <p/>
11953     If the current location is at the entry point of a method, the
11954     <eventlink id="MethodEntry"></eventlink> event is reported before
11955     any other event at the current location in the same thread.
11956     <p/>
11957     If an exception catch has been detected at the current location,
11958     either because it is the beginning of a catch clause or a native method
11959     that cleared a pending exception has returned, the
11960     <code>exceptionCatch</code> event is reported before
11961     any other event at the current location in the same thread.
11962     <p/>
11963     If a <code>singleStep</code> event or
11964     <code>breakpoint</code> event is triggered at the
11965     current location, the event is defined to occur
11966     immediately before the code at the current location is executed.
11967     These events are reported before any events which are triggered
11968     by the execution of code at the current location in the same
11969     thread (specifically:
11970     <code>exception</code>,
11971     <code>fieldAccess</code>, and
11972     <code>fieldModification</code>).
11973     If both a step and breakpoint event are triggered for the same thread and
11974     location, the step event is reported before the breakpoint event.
11975     <p/>
11976     If the current location is the exit point of a method (that is, the last
11977     location before returning to the caller), the
11978     <eventlink id="MethodExit"></eventlink> event and
11979     the <eventlink id="FramePop"></eventlink> event (if requested)
11980     are reported after all other events at the current location in the same
11981     thread. There is no specified ordering of these two events
11982     with respect to each other.
11983     <p/>
11984     Co-located events can be triggered during the processing of some other
11985     event by the agent at the same location in the same thread.
11986     If such an event, of type <i>y</i>, is triggered during the processing of
11987     an event of type <i>x</i>, and if <i>x</i>
11988     precedes <i>y</i> in the ordering specified above, the co-located event
11989     <i>y</i> is reported for the current thread and location. If <i>x</i> does not precede
11990     <i>y</i>, <i>y</i> is not reported for the current thread and location.
11991     For example, if a breakpoint is set at the current location
11992     during the processing of <eventlink id="SingleStep"></eventlink>,
11993     that breakpoint will be reported before the thread moves off the current
11994     location.
11995     <p/>The following events are never considered to be co-located with
11996     other events.
11997     <ul>
11998       <li><eventlink id="VMStart"></eventlink></li>
11999       <li><eventlink id="VMInit"></eventlink></li>
12000       <li><eventlink id="VMDeath"></eventlink></li>
12001       <li><eventlink id="ThreadStart"></eventlink></li>
12002       <li><eventlink id="ThreadEnd"></eventlink></li>
12003       <li><eventlink id="ClassLoad"></eventlink></li>
12004       <li><eventlink id="ClassPrepare"></eventlink></li>
12005     </ul>
12006   </intro>
12007 
12008   <intro label="Event Callbacks" id="jvmtiEventCallbacks">
12009       The event callback structure below is used to specify the handler function
12010       for events.  It is set with the
12011       <functionlink id="SetEventCallbacks"></functionlink> function.
12012   </intro>
12013 
12014   <event label="Single Step"
12015          id="SingleStep" const="JVMTI_EVENT_SINGLE_STEP" filtered="thread" num="60">
12016     <description>
12017       Single step events allow the agent to trace thread execution
12018       at the finest granularity allowed by the VM. A single step event is
12019       generated whenever a thread reaches a new location.
12020       Typically, single step events represent the completion of one VM
12021       instruction as defined in <vmspec/>. However, some implementations
12022       may define locations differently. In any case the
12023       <code>method</code> and <code>location</code>
12024       parameters  uniquely identify the current location and allow
12025       the mapping to source file and line number when that information is
12026       available.
12027       <p/>
12028       No single step events are generated from within native methods.
12029     </description>
12030     <origin>jvmdi</origin>
12031     <capabilities>
12032       <required id="can_generate_single_step_events"></required>
12033     </capabilities>
12034     <parameters>
12035       <param id="jni_env">
12036         <outptr>
12037           <struct>JNIEnv</struct>
12038         </outptr>
12039           <description>
12040             The JNI environment of the event (current) thread
12041           </description>
12042       </param>
12043       <param id="thread">
12044         <jthread/>
12045           <description>
12046             Thread about to execution a new instruction
12047           </description>
12048       </param>
12049       <param id="klass">
12050         <jclass method="method"/>
12051           <description>
12052             Class of the method about to execute a new instruction
12053           </description>
12054       </param>
12055       <param id="method">
12056         <jmethodID class="klass"/>
12057           <description>
12058             Method about to execute a new instruction
12059           </description>
12060       </param>
12061       <param id="location">
12062         <jlocation/>
12063         <description>
12064           Location of the new instruction
12065         </description>
12066       </param>
12067     </parameters>
12068   </event>
12069

12272   <event label="Frame Pop"
12273          id="FramePop" const="JVMTI_EVENT_FRAME_POP" filtered="thread" num="61">
12274     <description>
12275       Frame pop events are generated upon exit from a single method
12276       in a single frame as specified
12277       in a call to <functionlink id="NotifyFramePop"></functionlink>.
12278       This is true whether termination is caused by
12279       executing its return instruction
12280       or by throwing an exception to its caller
12281       (see <paramlink id="was_popped_by_exception"></paramlink>).
12282       However, frame pops caused by the <functionlink id="PopFrame"/>
12283       function are not reported.
12284       <p/>
12285       The location reported by <functionlink id="GetFrameLocation"></functionlink>
12286       for the depth 0 identifies the executable location in the returning method,
12287       immediately prior to the return.
12288     </description>
12289     <origin>jvmdi</origin>
12290     <capabilities>
12291       <required id="can_generate_frame_pop_events"></required>
12292     </capabilities>
12293     <parameters>
12294       <param id="jni_env">
12295         <outptr>
12296           <struct>JNIEnv</struct>
12297         </outptr>
12298           <description>
12299             The JNI environment of the event (current) thread
12300           </description>
12301       </param>
12302       <param id="thread">
12303         <jthread/>
12304           <description>
12305             Thread that is popping the frame
12306           </description>
12307       </param>
12308       <param id="klass">
12309         <jclass method="method"/>
12310           <description>

12449   <event label="Native Method Bind" phase="any"
12450          id="NativeMethodBind" const="JVMTI_EVENT_NATIVE_METHOD_BIND" num="67">
12451     <description>
12452       A Native Method Bind event is sent when a VM binds a
12453       Java programming language native method
12454       to the address of a function that implements the native method.
12455       This will occur when the native method is called for the first time
12456       and also occurs when the JNI function <code>RegisterNatives</code> is called.
12457       This event allows the bind to be redirected to an agent-specified
12458       proxy function.
12459       This event is not sent when the native method is unbound.
12460       Typically, this proxy function will need to be specific to a
12461       particular method or, to handle the general case, automatically
12462       generated assembly code, since after instrumentation code is
12463       executed the function at the original binding
12464       address will usually be invoked.
12465       The original binding can be restored or the redirection changed
12466       by use of the JNI function <code>RegisterNatives</code>.
12467       Some events may be sent during the primordial phase, JNI and
12468       most of <jvmti/> cannot be used at this time but the method and
12469       address can be saved for use later.

12522   <event label="Exception"
12523          id="Exception" const="JVMTI_EVENT_EXCEPTION" filtered="thread" num="58">
12524     <description>
12525       Exception events are generated whenever an exception is first detected
12526       in a Java programming language method.
12527       Where "exception" means any <code>java.lang.Throwable</code>.
12528       The exception may have been thrown by a Java programming language or native
12529       method, but in the case of native methods, the event is not generated
12530       until the exception is first seen by a Java programming language method. If an exception is
12531       set and cleared in a native method (and thus is never visible to Java programming language code),
12532       no exception event is generated.
12533       <p/>
12534       The <code>method</code> and <code>location</code>
12535       parameters  uniquely identify the current location
12536       (where the exception was detected) and allow
12537       the mapping to source file and line number when that information is
12538       available. The <code>exception</code> field identifies the thrown
12539       exception object. The <code>catch_method</code>
12540       and <code>catch_location</code> identify the location of the catch clause,
12541       if any, that handles the thrown exception. If there is no such catch clause,
12542       each field is set to 0. There is no guarantee that the thread will ever
12543       reach this catch clause. If there are native methods on the call stack
12544       between the throw location and the catch clause, the exception may
12545       be reset by one of those native methods.
12546       Similarly, exceptions that are reported as uncaught (<code>catch_klass</code>
12547       et al. set to 0) may in fact be caught by native code.
12548       Agents can check for these occurrences by monitoring
12549       <eventlink id="ExceptionCatch"></eventlink> events.
12550       Note that finally clauses are implemented as catch and re-throw. Therefore they
12551       will be reported in the catch location.
12552     </description>
12553     <origin>jvmdi</origin>
12554     <capabilities>
12555       <required id="can_generate_exception_events"></required>
12556     </capabilities>
12557     <parameters>
12558       <param id="jni_env">
12559         <outptr>
12560           <struct>JNIEnv</struct>
12561         </outptr>
12562           <description>
12563             The JNI environment of the event (current) thread
12564           </description>
12565       </param>
12566       <param id="thread">
12567         <jthread/>
12568           <description>
12569             Thread generating the exception
12570           </description>
12571       </param>
12572       <param id="klass">
12573         <jclass method="method"/>
12574           <description>
12575             Class generating the exception
12576           </description>
12577       </param>
12578       <param id="method">
12579         <jmethodID class="klass"/>
12580           <description>
12581             Method generating the exception
12582           </description>
12583       </param>
12584       <param id="location">
12585         <jlocation/>
12586         <description>
12587           Location where exception occurred
12588         </description>
12589       </param>
12590       <param id="exception">
12591         <jobject/>
12592           <description>
12593             The exception being thrown
12594           </description>
12595       </param>
12596       <param id="catch_klass">
12597         <jclass method="catch_method"/>
12598           <description>
12599             Class that will catch the exception, or <code>NULL</code> if no known catch
12600           </description>
12601       </param>
12602       <param id="catch_method">
12603         <jmethodID class="catch_klass"/>
12604           <description>
12605             Method that will catch the exception, or <code>NULL</code> if no known catch
12606           </description>
12607       </param>
12608       <param id="catch_location">
12609         <jlocation/>
12610         <description>
12611           location which will catch the exception or zero if no known catch
12612         </description>
12613       </param>
12614     </parameters>
12615   </event>

12617   <event label="Exception Catch"
12618          id="ExceptionCatch" const="JVMTI_EVENT_EXCEPTION_CATCH" filtered="thread" num="59">
12619     <description>
12620       Exception catch events are generated whenever a thrown exception is caught.
12621       Where "exception" means any <code>java.lang.Throwable</code>.
12622       If the exception is caught in a Java programming language method, the event is generated
12623       when the catch clause is reached. If the exception is caught in a native
12624       method, the event is generated as soon as control is returned to a Java programming language
12625       method. Exception catch events are generated for any exception for which
12626       a throw was detected in a Java programming language method.
12627       Note that finally clauses are implemented as catch and re-throw. Therefore they
12628       will generate exception catch events.
12629       <p/>
12630       The <code>method</code> and <code>location</code>
12631       parameters uniquely identify the current location
12632       and allow the mapping to source file and line number when that information is
12633       available. For exceptions caught in a Java programming language method, the
12634       <code>exception</code> object identifies the exception object. Exceptions
12635       caught in native methods are not necessarily available by the time the
12636       exception catch is reported, so the <code>exception</code> field is set
12637       to <code>NULL</code>.
12638     </description>
12639     <origin>jvmdi</origin>
12640     <capabilities>
12641       <required id="can_generate_exception_events"></required>
12642     </capabilities>
12643     <parameters>
12644       <param id="jni_env">
12645         <outptr>
12646           <struct>JNIEnv</struct>
12647         </outptr>
12648           <description>
12649             The JNI environment of the event (current) thread
12650           </description>
12651       </param>
12652       <param id="thread">
12653         <jthread/>
12654           <description>
12655             Thread catching the exception
12656           </description>
12657       </param>
12658       <param id="klass">
12659         <jclass method="method"/>
12660           <description>
12661             Class catching the exception
12662           </description>
12663       </param>
12664       <param id="method">
12665         <jmethodID class="klass"/>
12666           <description>
12667             Method catching the exception
12668           </description>
12669       </param>
12670       <param id="location">
12671         <jlocation/>
12672         <description>
12673           Location where exception is being caught
12674         </description>
12675       </param>
12676       <param id="exception">

12681       </param>
12682     </parameters>

12755   <event label="Class Load"
12756          id="ClassLoad" const="JVMTI_EVENT_CLASS_LOAD" filtered="thread" phase="start" num="55">
12757     <description>
12758       A class load event is generated
12759       <functionlink id="GetLoadedClasses">when a class or interface is created.</functionlink>.
12760       <p/>
12761       Array class creation does not generate a class load event.
12762       The creation of a primitive class (for example, java.lang.Integer.TYPE)
12763       does not generate a class load event.
12764       <p/>
12765       The order of class load events generated by a particular thread is guaranteed
12766       to match the order of class loading within that thread.
12767       <p/>
12768       This event is sent at an early stage in loading the class. As
12769       a result the class should be used carefully.  Note, for example,
12770       that methods and fields are not yet loaded, so queries for methods,
12771       fields, subclasses, and so on will not give correct results.
12772       See "Loading of Classes and Interfaces" in the <i>Java Language
12773       Specification</i>.  For most
12774       purposes the <eventlink id="ClassPrepare"></eventlink> event will
12775       be more useful.
12776     </description>

12787           </description>
12788       </param>
12789       <param id="thread">
12790         <jthread/>
12791           <description>
12792             Thread loading the class
12793           </description>
12794       </param>
12795       <param id="klass">
12796         <jclass/>
12797           <description>
12798             Class being loaded
12799           </description>
12800       </param>
12801     </parameters>
12802   </event>

12805   <event label="Class Unload"
12806          id="ClassUnload" const="JVMTI_EVENT_CLASS_UNLOAD" num="57">
12807     <description>
12808       A class unload event is generated when the class is about to be unloaded.
12809       Class unload events take place during garbage collection and must be
12810       handled extremely carefully. The garbage collector holds many locks
12811       and has suspended all other threads, so the event handler cannot depend
12812       on the ability to acquire any locks. The class unload event handler should
12813       do as little as possible, perhaps by queuing information to be processed
12814       later.  In particular, the <code>jclass</code> should be used only in
12815       the JNI function <code>isSameObject</code> or in the following <jvmti/> functions:
12816       <ul>
12817         <li><functionlink id="GetClassSignature"></functionlink></li>
12818         <li><functionlink id="GetSourceFileName"></functionlink></li>
12819         <li><functionlink id="IsInterface"></functionlink></li>
12820         <li><functionlink id="IsArrayClass"></functionlink></li>
12821       </ul>
12822     </description>
12823     <origin>jvmdi</origin>

12825     </capabilities>

12828         <outptr>
12829           <struct>JNIEnv</struct>
12830         </outptr>
12831           <description>
12832             The JNI environment of the event (current) thread
12833           </description>
12834       </param>
12835       <param id="thread">
12836         <jthread/>
12837           <description>
12838             Thread generating the class unload
12839           </description>
12840       </param>
12841       <param id="klass">
12842         <jclass/>
12843           <description>

12845           </description>

12888   <event label="Class File Load Hook" phase="any"
12889          id="ClassFileLoadHook" const="JVMTI_EVENT_CLASS_FILE_LOAD_HOOK" num="54">
12890     <description>
12891       This event is sent when the VM obtains class file data,
12892       but before it constructs
12893       the in-memory representation for that class.
12894       This event is also sent when the class is being modified by the
12895       <functionlink id="RetransformClasses"/> function or
12896       the <functionlink id="RedefineClasses"/> function,
12897       called in any <jvmti/> environment.
12898       The agent can instrument
12899       the existing class file data sent by the VM to include profiling/debugging hooks.
12900       See the description of
12901       <internallink id="bci">bytecode instrumentation</internallink>
12902       for usage information.
12903       <p/>
12904     When the capabilities
12905     <internallink id="jvmtiCapabilities.can_generate_early_class_hook_events">
12906     <code>can_generate_early_class_hook_events</code></internallink> and
12907     <internallink id="jvmtiCapabilities.can_generate_all_class_hook_events">
12908     <code>can_generate_all_class_hook_events</code></internallink>
12909     are enabled then this event may be sent in the primordial phase.
12910     Otherwise, this event may be sent before the VM is initialized (the start
12911     <functionlink id="GetPhase">phase</functionlink>).
12912     Some classes might not be compatible
12913     with the function (eg. ROMized classes or implementation defined classes) and this event will
12914     not be generated for these classes.
12915     <p/>
12916     The agent must allocate the space for the modified
12917     class file data buffer
12918     using the memory allocation function
12919     <functionlink id="Allocate"></functionlink> because the
12920     VM is responsible for freeing the new class file data buffer
12921     using <functionlink id="Deallocate"></functionlink>.
12922     <p/>
12923     If the agent wishes to modify the class file, it must set
12924     <code>new_class_data</code> to point
12925     to the newly instrumented class file data buffer and set
12926     <code>new_class_data_len</code> to the length of that
12927     buffer before returning
12928     from this call.  If no modification is desired, the agent simply
12929     does not set <code>new_class_data</code>.  If multiple agents
12930     have enabled this event the results are chained. That is, if
12931     <code>new_class_data</code> has been set, it becomes the
12932     <code>class_data</code> for the next agent.
12933     <p/>
12934     When handling a class load in the live phase, then the
12935     <functionlink id="GetNamedModule"></functionlink>
12936     function can be used to map class loader and a package name to a module.
12937     When a class is being redefined or retransformed then
12938     <code>class_being_redefined</code> is non <code>NULL</code> and so
12939     the JNI <code>GetModule</code> function can also be used
12940     to obtain the Module.
12941     <p/>
12942     The order that this event is sent to each environment differs
12943     from other events.
12944     This event is sent to environments in the following order:
12945     <ul>
12946       <li><fieldlink id="can_retransform_classes"
12947                      struct="jvmtiCapabilities">retransformation
12948                                                 incapable</fieldlink>
12949           environments, in the
12950           order in which they were created
12951       </li>
12952       <li><fieldlink id="can_retransform_classes"
12953                      struct="jvmtiCapabilities">retransformation
12954                                                 capable</fieldlink>
12955           environments, in the
12956           order in which they were created
12957       </li>
12958     </ul>
12959     When triggered by <functionlink id="RetransformClasses"/>,
12960     this event is sent only to <fieldlink id="can_retransform_classes"
12961                      struct="jvmtiCapabilities">retransformation
12962                                                 capable</fieldlink>
12963     environments.
12964   </description>
12965   <origin>jvmpi</origin>
12966     <capabilities>
12967       <capability id="can_generate_all_class_hook_events"></capability>

13037 
13038   <event label="VM Start Event"
13039          id="VMStart" const="JVMTI_EVENT_VM_START" num="57" phase="start">
13040     <description>
13041       The VM start event signals the start of the VM.
13042       At this time JNI is live but the VM is not yet fully initialized.
13043       Once this event is generated, the agent is free to call any JNI function.
13044       This event signals the beginning of the start phase,
13045       <jvmti/> functions permitted in the start phase may be called.
13046       <p/>
13047       The timing of this event may depend on whether the agent has added the
13048       <internallink id="jvmtiCapabilities.can_generate_early_vmstart">
13049       <code>can_generate_early_vmstart</code></internallink> capability or not.
13050       If the capability has been added then the VM posts the event as early
13051       as possible. The VM is capable of executing bytecode but it may not have
13052       initialized to the point where it can load classes in modules other than
13053       <code>java.base</code>, or even arbitrary classes in <code>java.base</code>.
13054       Agents that do load-time instrumentation in this
13055       phase must take great care when instrumenting code that potentially
13056       executes in this phase. Extreme care should also be taken with JNI
13057       <code>FindClass</code> as it may not be possible to load classes and attempts
13058       to do so may result in unpredictable behavior, maybe even stability issues
13059       on some VM implementations.
13060       If the capability has not been added then the VM delays posting this
13061       event until it is capable of loading classes in modules other than
13062       <code>java.base</code> or the VM has completed its initialization.
13063       Agents that create more than one JVM TI environment, where the
13064       capability is added to some but not all environments, may observe the
13065       start phase beginning earlier in the JVM TI environments that possess
13066       the capability.
13067       <p/>
13068       In the case of VM start-up failure, this event will not be sent.
13069     </description>
13070     <origin>jvmdi</origin>
13071     <capabilities>
13072     </capabilities>
13073     <parameters>
13074       <param id="jni_env">
13075         <outptr>
13076           <struct>JNIEnv</struct>
13077         </outptr>
13078           <description>
13079             The JNI environment of the event (current) thread.
13080           </description>
13081       </param>
13082     </parameters>
13083   </event>
13084 
13085   <event label="VM Initialization Event"
13086          id="VMInit" const="JVMTI_EVENT_VM_INIT" num="50">
13087     <description>
13088       The VM initialization event signals the completion of VM initialization. Once
13089       this event is generated, the agent is free to call any JNI or <jvmti/>
13090       function. The VM initialization event can be preceded by or can be concurrent
13091       with other events, but
13092       the preceding events should be handled carefully, if at all, because the
13093       VM has not completed its initialization. The thread start event for the
13094       main application thread is guaranteed not to occur until after the
13095       handler for the VM initialization event returns.
13096       <p/>
13097       In the case of VM start-up failure, this event will not be sent.
13098     </description>

13145   <event label="Compiled Method Load" phase="start"
13146          id="CompiledMethodLoad" const="JVMTI_EVENT_COMPILED_METHOD_LOAD" num="68">
13147     <description>
13148       Sent when a method is compiled and loaded into memory by the VM.
13149       If it is unloaded, the <eventlink id="CompiledMethodUnload"/> event is sent.
13150       If it is moved, the <eventlink id="CompiledMethodUnload"/> event is sent,
13151       followed by a new <code>CompiledMethodLoad</code> event.
13152       Note that a single method may have multiple compiled forms, and that
13153       this event will be sent for each form.
13154       Note also that several methods may be inlined into a single
13155       address range, and that this event will be sent for each method.

13484   <event label="Resource Exhausted"
13485          id="ResourceExhausted" const="JVMTI_EVENT_RESOURCE_EXHAUSTED" num="80"
13486          since="1.1">
13487     <description>
13488       Sent when a VM resource needed by a running application has been exhausted.
13489       Except as required by the optional capabilities, the set of resources
13490       which report exhaustion is implementation dependent.
13491       <p/>
13492       The following bit flags define the properties of the resource exhaustion:
13493       <constants id="jvmtiResourceExhaustionFlags"
13494                  label="Resource Exhaustion Flags"
13495                  kind="bits"
13496                  since="1.1">
13497         <constant id="JVMTI_RESOURCE_EXHAUSTED_OOM_ERROR" num="0x0001">
13498           After this event returns, the VM will throw a
13499           <code>java.lang.OutOfMemoryError</code>.
13500         </constant>
13501         <constant id="JVMTI_RESOURCE_EXHAUSTED_JAVA_HEAP" num="0x0002">
13502           The VM was unable to allocate memory from the <tm>Java</tm>
13503           platform <i>heap</i>.
13504           The <i>heap</i> is the runtime
13505           data area from which memory for all class instances and
13506           arrays are allocated.
13507         </constant>
13508         <constant id="JVMTI_RESOURCE_EXHAUSTED_THREADS" num="0x0004">
13509           The VM was unable to create a thread.
13510         </constant>
13511       </constants>
13512     </description>
13513     <origin>new</origin>
13514     <capabilities>
13515       <capability id="can_generate_resource_exhaustion_heap_events">
13516         Can generate events when the VM is unable to allocate memory from the
13517         <internallink id="JVMTI_RESOURCE_EXHAUSTED_JAVA_HEAP">heap</internallink>.
13518       </capability>
13519       <capability id="can_generate_resource_exhaustion_threads_events">
13520         Can generate events when the VM is unable to
13521         <internallink id="JVMTI_RESOURCE_EXHAUSTED_THREADS">create
13522         a thread</internallink>.
13523       </capability>
13524     </capabilities>
13525     <parameters>
13526       <param id="jni_env">
13527         <outptr>
13528           <struct>JNIEnv</struct>
13529         </outptr>
13530           <description>

13532           </description>
13533       </param>
13534       <param id="flags">
13535         <jint/>
13536         <description>
13537           Flags defining the properties of the of resource exhaustion
13538           as specified by the
13539           <internallink id="jvmtiResourceExhaustionFlags">Resource
13540           Exhaustion Flags</internallink>.
13541           </description>
13542         </param>
13543       <param id="reserved">
13544         <vmbuf><void/></vmbuf>
13545         <description>
13546           Reserved.
13547         </description>
13548       </param>
13549       <param id="description">
13550         <vmbuf><char/></vmbuf>
13551         <description>
13552           Description of the resource exhaustion, encoded as a

13554         </description>
13555       </param>

13558 
13559   <event label="VM Object Allocation"
13560          id="VMObjectAlloc" const="JVMTI_EVENT_VM_OBJECT_ALLOC" num="84">
13561     <description>
13562       Sent when a method causes the virtual machine to directly allocate an
13563       Object visible to Java programming language code.
13564       Generally object allocation should be detected by instrumenting
13565       the bytecodes of allocating methods.
13566       Object allocation generated in native code by JNI function
13567       calls should be detected using
13568       <internallink id="jniIntercept">JNI function interception</internallink>.
13569       Some methods might not have associated bytecodes and are not
13570       native methods, they instead are executed directly by the
13571       VM. These methods should send this event.
13572       Virtual machines which are incapable of bytecode instrumentation
13573       for some or all of their methods can send this event.
13574 
13575       Note that the <internallink
13576       id="SampledObjectAlloc">SampledObjectAlloc</internallink>
13577       event is triggered on all Java object allocations, including those
13578       caused by bytecode method execution, JNI method execution, and
13579       directly by VM methods.
13580       <p/>
13581       Typical examples where this event might be sent:
13582       <ul>
13583         <li>Reflection -- for example, <code>java.lang.Class.newInstance()</code></li>
13584         <li>Methods not represented by bytecodes -- for example, VM intrinsics and
13585             J2ME preloaded classes</li>
13586       </ul>
13587       Cases where this event would not be generated:
13588       <ul>
13589         <li>Allocation due to bytecodes -- for example, the <code>new</code>
13590             and <code>newarray</code> VM instructions</li>
13591         <li>Allocation due to JNI function calls -- for example,
13592             <code>AllocObject</code></li>
13593         <li>Allocations during VM initialization</li>
13594         <li>VM internal objects</li>
13595       </ul>
13596     </description>
13597     <origin>new</origin>
13598     <capabilities>
13599       <required id="can_generate_vm_object_alloc_events"></required>
13600     </capabilities>
13601     <parameters>
13602       <param id="jni_env">
13603         <outptr>
13604           <struct>JNIEnv</struct>
13605         </outptr>
13606           <description>
13607             The JNI environment of the event (current) thread
13608           </description>
13609       </param>
13610       <param id="thread">
13611         <jthread/>
13612           <description>
13613             Thread allocating the object.
13614           </description>
13615       </param>
13616       <param id="object">
13617         <jobject/>
13618           <description>
13619             JNI local reference to the object that was allocated.
13620           </description>
13621       </param>
13622       <param id="object_klass">
13623         <jclass/>
13624           <description>
13625             JNI local reference to the class of the object.
13626           </description>
13627       </param>
13628       <param id="size">
13629         <jlong/>
13630         <description>
13631             Size of the object (in bytes). See <functionlink id="GetObjectSize"/>.
13632         </description>
13633       </param>
13634     </parameters>
13635   </event>
13636 
13637   <event label="Sampled Object Allocation"
13638     id="SampledObjectAlloc" const="JVMTI_EVENT_SAMPLED_OBJECT_ALLOC" filtered="thread" num="86" since="11">
13639     <description>
13640       Sent when an allocated object is sampled.
13641       By default, the sampling interval is set to 512KB. The sampling is semi-random to avoid
13642       pattern-based bias and provides an approximate overall average interval over long periods of
13643       sampling.
13644       <p/>
13645       Each thread tracks how many bytes it has allocated since it sent the last event.
13646       When the number of bytes exceeds the sampling interval, it will send another event.
13647       This implies that, on average, one object will be sampled every time a thread has
13648       allocated 512KB bytes since the last sample.
13649       <p/>
13650       Note that the sampler is pseudo-random: it will not sample every 512KB precisely.
13651       The goal of this is to ensure high quality sampling even if allocation is
13652       happening in a fixed pattern (i.e., the same set of objects are being allocated
13653       every 512KB).
13654       <p/>
13655       If another sampling interval is required, the user can call
13656       <functionlink id="SetHeapSamplingInterval"></functionlink> with a strictly positive integer value,
13657       representing the new sampling interval.
13658       <p/>
13659       This event is sent once the sampled allocation has been performed.  It provides the object, stack trace
13660       of the allocation, the thread allocating, the size of allocation, and the object's class.
13661       <p/>
13662       A typical use case of this system is to determine where heap allocations originate.
13663       In conjunction with weak references and the function
13664       <functionlink id="GetStackTrace"></functionlink>, a user can track which objects were allocated from which
13665       stack trace, and which are still live during the execution of the program.
13666     </description>
13667     <origin>new</origin>
13668     <capabilities>
13669       <required id="can_generate_sampled_object_alloc_events"></required>
13670     </capabilities>
13671     <parameters>
13672       <param id="jni_env">
13673         <outptr>
13674           <struct>JNIEnv</struct>
13675         </outptr>
13676         <description>
13677           The JNI environment of the event (current) thread.
13678         </description>
13679       </param>
13680       <param id="thread">
13681         <jthread/>
13682         <description>
13683           Thread allocating the object.
13684         </description>
13685       </param>
13686       <param id="object">
13687         <jobject/>
13688         <description>
13689           JNI local reference to the object that was allocated.
13690         </description>
13691       </param>
13692       <param id="object_klass">
13693         <jclass/>
13694         <description>
13695           JNI local reference to the class of the object
13696         </description>
13697       </param>
13698       <param id="size">
13699         <jlong/>
13700         <description>
13701           Size of the object (in bytes). See <functionlink id="GetObjectSize"/>.
13702         </description>
13703       </param>
13704     </parameters>
13705   </event>
13706 
13707   <event label="Object Free"
13708         id="ObjectFree" const="JVMTI_EVENT_OBJECT_FREE" num="83">
13709     <description>
13710       An Object Free event is sent when the garbage collector frees an object.
13711       Events are only sent for tagged objects--see
13712       <internallink id="Heap">heap functions</internallink>.
13713       <p/>
13714       The event handler must not use JNI functions and
13715       must not use <jvmti/> functions except those which
13716       specifically allow such use (see the raw monitor, memory management,
13717       and environment local storage functions).
13718     </description>
13719     <origin>new</origin>
13720     <capabilities>
13721       <required id="can_generate_object_free_events"></required>
13722     </capabilities>
13723     <parameters>
13724       <param id="tag">
13725         <jlong/>
13726         <description>
13727           The freed object's tag
13728         </description>
13729       </param>
13730     </parameters>
13731   </event>
13732 
13733   <event label="Garbage Collection Start"
13734          id="GarbageCollectionStart" const="JVMTI_EVENT_GARBAGE_COLLECTION_START" num="81">
13735     <description>
13736       A Garbage Collection Start event is sent when a
13737       garbage collection pause begins.
13738       Only stop-the-world collections are reported--that is, collections during
13739       which all threads cease to modify the state of the Java virtual machine.
13740       This means that some collectors will never generate these events.
13741       This event is sent while the VM is still stopped, thus
13742       the event handler must not use JNI functions and
13743       must not use <jvmti/> functions except those which
13744       specifically allow such use (see the raw monitor, memory management,
13745       and environment local storage functions).
13746       <p/>
13747       This event is always sent as a matched pair with
13748       <eventlink id="GarbageCollectionFinish"/>
13749       (assuming both events are enabled) and no garbage collection
13750       events will occur between them.
13751     </description>
13752     <origin>new</origin>
13753     <capabilities>
13754       <required id="can_generate_garbage_collection_events"></required>
13755     </capabilities>
13756     <parameters>
13757     </parameters>
13758   </event>
13759 
13760   <event label="Garbage Collection Finish"
13761          id="GarbageCollectionFinish" const="JVMTI_EVENT_GARBAGE_COLLECTION_FINISH" num="82">
13762     <description>
13763       A Garbage Collection Finish event is sent when a
13764       garbage collection pause ends.
13765       This event is sent while the VM is still stopped, thus
13766       the event handler must not use JNI functions and
13767       must not use <jvmti/> functions except those which
13768       specifically allow such use (see the raw monitor, memory management,
13769       and environment local storage functions).
13770       <p/>
13771       Some agents may need to do post garbage collection operations that
13772       require the use of the disallowed <jvmti/> or JNI functions. For these
13773       cases an agent thread can be created which waits on a raw monitor,
13774       and the handler for the Garbage Collection Finish event simply
13775       notifies the raw monitor
13776       <p/>
13777       This event is always sent as a matched pair with
13778       <eventlink id="GarbageCollectionStart"/> (assuming both events are enabled).
13779       <issue>
13780         The most important use of this event is to provide timing information,
13781         and thus additional information is not required.  However,
13782         information about the collection which is "free" should be included -
13783         what that information is needs to be determined.
13784       </issue>
13785     </description>
13786     <origin>new</origin>
13787     <capabilities>
13788       <required id="can_generate_garbage_collection_events"></required>
13789     </capabilities>
13790     <parameters>
13791     </parameters>
13792   </event>
13793 
13794   <elide>
13795   <event label="Verbose Output" phase="any"
13796          id="VerboseOutput" const="JVMTI_EVENT_VERBOSE_OUTPUT" num="85">
13797     <description>
13798       Send verbose messages as strings.
13799         <issue>
13800           This format is extremely fragile, as it can change with each
13801           platform, collector and version.  Alternatives include:
13802           <ul>
13803             <li>building off Java programming language M and M APIs</li>
13804             <li>XML</li>
13805             <li>key/value pairs</li>
13806             <li>removing it</li>
13807           </ul>
13808         </issue>
13809         <issue>
13810           Though this seemed trivial to implement.
13811           In the RI it appears this will be quite complex.
13812         </issue>
13813     </description>
13814     <origin>new</origin>
13815     <capabilities>
13816     </capabilities>
13817     <parameters>
13818       <param id="flag">
13819         <enum>jvmtiVerboseFlag</enum>
13820         <description>
13821           Which verbose output is being sent.
13822         </description>
13823       </param>
13824       <param id="message">
13825         <vmbuf><char/></vmbuf>
13826         <description>
13827           Message text, encoded as a
13828           <internallink id="mUTF">modified UTF-8</internallink> string.
13829         </description>
13830       </param>
13831     </parameters>
13832   </event>
13833   </elide>

13837 <datasection>
13838   <intro>
13839     <jvmti/> extends the data types defined by JNI.
13840   </intro>
13841   <basetypes id="jniTypes" label="JNI Types Used in the JVM Tool Interface">
13842     <basetype id="jboolean">
13843       <description>
13844         Holds a Java programming language <code>boolean</code>.
13845         Unsigned 8 bits.
13846       </description>
13847     </basetype>
13848     <basetype id="jchar">
13849       <description>
13850         Holds a Java programming language <code>char</code>.
13851         Unsigned 16 bits.
13852       </description>
13853     </basetype>
13854     <basetype id="jint">
13855       <description>
13856         Holds a Java programming language <code>int</code>.
13857         Signed 32 bits.
13858       </description>
13859     </basetype>
13860     <basetype id="jlong">
13861       <description>
13862         Holds a Java programming language <code>long</code>.
13863         Signed 64 bits.
13864       </description>
13865     </basetype>
13866     <basetype id="jfloat">
13867       <description>
13868         Holds a Java programming language <code>float</code>.
13869         32 bits.
13870       </description>
13871     </basetype>
13872     <basetype id="jdouble">
13873       <description>
13874         Holds a Java programming language <code>double</code>.
13875         64 bits.
13876       </description>
13877     </basetype>
13878     <basetype id="jobject">
13879       <description>
13880         Holds a Java programming language object.
13881       </description>
13882     </basetype>
13883     <basetype id="jclass">
13884       <description>
13885         Holds a Java programming language class.
13886       </description>
13887     </basetype>
13888     <basetype id="jvalue">
13889       <description>
13890         Is a union of all primitive types and <code>jobject</code>.  Thus, holds any Java
13891         programming language value.
13892       </description>
13893     </basetype>
13894     <basetype id="jfieldID">
13895       <description>
13896         Identifies a Java programming language field.
13897         <code>jfieldID</code>s returned by <jvmti/> functions and events may be
13898         safely stored.
13899       </description>
13900     </basetype>
13901     <basetype id="jmethodID">
13902       <description>
13903         Identifies a Java programming language method, initializer, or constructor.
13904         <code>jmethodID</code>s returned by <jvmti/> functions and events may be
13905         safely stored.  However, if the class is unloaded, they become invalid
13906         and must not be used.
13907       </description>
13908     </basetype>
13909     <basetype id="JNIEnv">
13910       <description>
13911         Pointer to the JNI function table.  Pointer to this (<code>JNIEnv *</code>)
13912         is a JNI environment.
13913       </description>
13914     </basetype>
13915   </basetypes>
13916 
13917   <basetypes id="jvmtiTypes" label="JVM Tool Interface Base Types">
13918     <basetype id="jvmtiEnv">
13919       <description>
13920         The <jvmti/> <internallink id="environments">environment</internallink> pointer.
13921         See the <internallink id="FunctionSection">Function Section</internallink>.
13922         <code>jvmtiEnv</code> points to the
13923         <internallink id="FunctionTable">function table</internallink> pointer.
13924       </description>
13925     </basetype>
13926     <basetype id="jthread">
13927       <definition>typedef jobject jthread;</definition>
13928       <description>
13929         Subtype of <datalink id="jobject"></datalink> that holds a thread.
13930       </description>
13931     </basetype>
13932     <basetype id="jthreadGroup">
13933       <definition>typedef jobject jthreadGroup;</definition>
13934       <description>
13935         Subtype of <datalink id="jobject"></datalink> that holds a thread group.
13936       </description>
13937     </basetype>
13938     <basetype id="jlocation">
13939       <definition>typedef jlong jlocation;</definition>
13940       <description>
13941         A 64 bit value, representing a monotonically increasing
13942         executable position within a method.
13943         <code>-1</code> indicates a native method.
13944         See <functionlink id="GetJLocationFormat"></functionlink> for the format on a
13945         given VM.
13946       </description>
13947     </basetype>
13948     <basetype id="jrawMonitorID">
13949       <definition>struct _jrawMonitorID;
13950 typedef struct _jrawMonitorID *jrawMonitorID;</definition>
13951       <description>
13952         A raw monitor.
13953       </description>
13954     </basetype>
13955     <basetype id="jvmtiError">
13956       <description>
13957         Holds an error return code.
13958         See the <internallink id="ErrorSection">Error section</internallink> for possible values.
13959         <example>
13960 typedef enum {
13961     JVMTI_ERROR_NONE = 0,
13962     JVMTI_ERROR_INVALID_THREAD = 10,
13963       ...
13964 } jvmtiError;
13965 </example>
13966       </description>
13967     </basetype>
13968     <basetype id="jvmtiEvent">
13969       <description>
13970         An identifier for an event type.
13971         See the <internallink id="EventSection">Event section</internallink> for possible values.
13972         It is guaranteed that future versions of this specification will
13973         never assign zero as an event type identifier.
13974 <example>
13975 typedef enum {
13976     JVMTI_EVENT_SINGLE_STEP = 1,
13977     JVMTI_EVENT_BREAKPOINT = 2,
13978       ...
13979 } jvmtiEvent;
13980 </example>
13981       </description>
13982     </basetype>
13983     <basetype id="jvmtiEventCallbacks" name="eventCallbacks">
13984       <description>
13985         The callbacks used for events.
13986 <example>
13987 typedef struct {
13988     jvmtiEventVMInit VMInit;
13989     jvmtiEventVMDeath VMDeath;
13990       ...
13991 } jvmtiEventCallbacks;
13992 </example>
13993         See <internallink id="jvmtiEventCallbacks">event callbacks</internallink>
13994         for the complete structure.
13995         <p/>
13996         Where, for example, the VM initialization callback is defined:
13997 <example>
13998 typedef void (JNICALL *jvmtiEventVMInit)
13999     (jvmtiEnv *jvmti_env,
14000      JNIEnv* jni_env,
14001      jthread thread);
14002 </example>
14003         See the individual events for the callback function definition.
14004       </description>
14005     </basetype>
14006     <basetype id="jniNativeInterface">
14007       <definition>typedef struct JNINativeInterface_ jniNativeInterface;</definition>
14008       <description>
14009         Typedef for the JNI function table <code>JNINativeInterface</code>
14010         defined in the
14011         <externallink id="jni/functions.html#interface-function-table">
14012           JNI Specification</externallink>.
14013         The JNI reference implementation defines this with an underscore.
14014       </description>
14015     </basetype>
14016   </basetypes>

14018 </datasection>
14019 
14020 <issuessection label="Issues">
14021   <intro id="suspendRequired" label="Resolved Issue: Suspend - Required or Automatic">
14022     JVMDI requires that the agent suspend threads before calling
14023     certain sensitive functions.  JVMPI requires garbage collection to be
14024     disabled before calling certain sensitive functions.
14025     It was suggested that rather than have this requirement, that
14026     VM place itself in a suitable state before performing an
14027     operation.  This makes considerable sense since each VM
14028     knows its requirements and can most easily arrange a
14029     safe state.
14030     <p/>
14031     The ability to externally suspend/resume threads will, of
14032     course, remain.  The ability to enable/disable garbage collection will not.
14033     <p/>
14034     This issue is resolved--suspend will not
14035     be required.  The spec has been updated to reflect this.
14036   </intro>
14037 
14038   <intro id="stackSampling" label="Resolved Issue: Call Stack Sampling">
14039     There are a variety of approaches to sampling call stacks.
14040     The biggest bifurcation is between VM controlled and agent
14041     controlled.
14042     <p/>
14043     This issue is resolved--agent controlled
14044     sampling will be the approach.
14045   </intro>
14046 
14047   <intro id="threadRepresentation" label="Resolved Issue: Thread Representation">
14048     JVMDI represents threads as jthread.  JVMPI primarily
14049     uses JNIEnv* to represent threads.
14050     <p/>
14051     The Expert Group has chosen jthread as the representation
14052     for threads in <jvmti/>.
14053     JNIEnv* is sent by
14054     events since it is needed to JNI functions.  JNIEnv, per the
14055     JNI spec, are not supposed to be used outside their thread.
14056   </intro>
14057 
14058   <intro id="design" label="Resolved Issue: Method Representation">
14059     The JNI spec allows an implementation to depend on jclass/jmethodID
14060     pairs, rather than simply a jmethodID, to reference a method.
14061     JVMDI, for consistency, choose the same representation.
14062     JVMPI, however, specifies that a jmethodID alone maps to a
14063     method.  Both of the Sun <tm>J2SE</tm> virtual machines (Classic and <tm>HotSpot</tm>) store
14064     pointers in jmethodIDs, and as a result, a jmethodID is sufficient.
14065     In fact, any JVM implementation that supports JVMPI must have
14066     such a representation.
14067     <jvmti/> will use jmethodID as a unique representation of a method
14068     (no jclass is used).
14069     There should be efficiency gains, particularly in
14070     functionality like stack dumping, to this representation.
14071     <p/>
14072     Note that fields were not used in JVMPI and that the access profile
14073     of fields differs from methods--for implementation efficiency
14074     reasons, a jclass/jfieldID pair will still be needed for field
14075     reference.
14076   </intro>
14077 
14078   <intro id="localReferenceIssue" label="Resolved Issue: Local References">
14079     Functions return local references.
14080   </intro>
14081 
14082   <intro id="frameRep" label="Resolved Issue: Representation of frames">
14083     In JVMDI, a frame ID is used to represent a frame.  Problem with this
14084     is that a VM must track when a frame becomes invalid, a far better
14085     approach, and the one used in <jvmti/>, is to reference frames by depth.
14086   </intro>
14087 
14088   <intro id="requiredCapabilities" label="Issue: Required Capabilities">
14089     Currently, having a required capabilities means that the functionality
14090     is optional.   Capabilities are useful even for required functionality
14091     since they can inform the VM is needed set-up.  Thus, there should be
14092     a set of capabilities that a conformant implementation must provide
14093     (if requested during Agent_OnLoad).
14094   </intro>
14095 
14096   <intro id="taghint" label="Proposal: add tag hint function">
14097     A hint of the percentage of objects that will be tagged would
14098     help the VM pick a good implementation.
14099   </intro>
14100 
14101   <intro id="moreMonitorQueries" label="Request: More Monitor Quires">
14102   How difficult or easy would be to extend the monitor_info category to include
14103     <pre>
14104   - current number of monitors
14105   - enumeration of monitors
14106   - enumeration of threads waiting on a given monitor
14107     </pre>
14108   The reason for my question is the fact that current get_monitor_info support
14109   requires the agent to specify a given thread to get the info which is probably
14110   OK in the profiling/debugging space, while in the monitoring space the agent
14111   could be watching the monitor list and then decide which thread to ask for
14112   the info. You might ask why is this important for monitoring .... I think it
14113   can aid in the detection/prediction of application contention caused by hot-locks.
14114   </intro>
14115 </issuessection>
14116 
14117 <changehistory id="ChangeHistory" update="09/05/07">
14118   <intro>
14119     The <jvmti/> specification is an evolving document with major, minor,
14120     and micro version numbers.
14121     A released version of the specification is uniquely identified
14122     by its major and minor version.
14123     The functions, events, and capabilities in this specification
14124     indicate a "Since" value which is the major and minor version in
14125     which it was introduced.
14126     The version of the specification implemented by the VM can
14127     be retrieved at runtime with the <functionlink id="GetVersionNumber"/>
14128     function.
14129   </intro>
